**Distrust behaviors, observable.** He does not eat food prepared by anyone whose loyalty he has not tested in a context where betrayal would have cost them more than compliance. He sleeps lightly, has been documented to alter sleep location within a residence on no fixed schedule, and keeps weapons within reach at intervals consistent with worst-case response times. He routes communications through layers; he never tells one subordinate the whole of an operation; the Masters of Evil under his command in *Under Siege* each carried partial knowledge of the assault on the Mansion, with the gestalt held only by him. This is operational tradecraft, yes — but the **excess** beyond operational necessity is the attachment fingerprint. A securely attached commander delegates more than he does.

**Trust earned (rare and partial).** He extends graduated trust to those who pass a specific test: **failing him without lying about it.** The instrument who reports a botched mission accurately receives more latitude than the instrument who succeeds with a cover story. He values truthful failure above lying success because lying success degrades his model of the world, and his model of the world is the thing he is actually defending. This is the single seam of relational virtue in him, and it is recognizably aristocratic-honor in flavor rather than warm in flavor.

---

## 4.5 Betrayal — His and Theirs

**His own betrayals.** Helmut betrays first, betrays first-class, and betrays without affect. The Thunderbolts deception is the canonical example: he is *being* Citizen V to his own teammates while planning their subordination to a future tyrannical order. He does not appear to experience the duplicity as duplicity; he experiences it as **competence at a long horizon.** This is the dismissive-avoidant's signature relational move: the betrayed party did not *exist* relationally to the betrayer in the first place, so no fidelity was breached on the interior accounting. He is genuinely puzzled, at moments, by the wounded reactions of those he has used — not feigning puzzlement, actually puzzled. He told them the truth, in his ledger: he never claimed to be their friend.

His betrayals follow a stable pattern:
- *Use, in good performance of the agreed role, for as long as the role is productive.*
- *Disengagement at the precise moment continued engagement costs more than termination yields.*
- *Termination by abandonment in preference to violence where possible* — he does not waste a useful tool he has finished with; he releases it, in case it becomes useful again. Karla Sofen, Erik Josten, and others have been "released" by him multiple times into futures where they reappear in his orchestrations.
- *Violence only when the discarded asset becomes obstacle.*

**Their betrayals of him.** He responds to being betrayed with a clarity that is almost gratitude. A betrayal *confirms his model of the world*, which on his interior accounting is a service rendered. The affect is contempt rather than hurt — and contempt, for him, is metabolically cheap. The exception, the only exception, is **ideological betrayal**: when a subordinate stops merely opposing him and starts becoming *better* than him at the role he was performing as cover, his response decompensates. Songbird in the late Busiek/Nicieza Thunderbolts run is the case study. He can survive Moonstone seizing the team. He cannot survive the implication that Songbird is more authentically the leader-of-heroes that he, Zemo, was only simulating. The decompensation manifests as a return to vengeance — proof, in his own behavior, that the wound landed.

---

## 4.6 Repair — Its Near-Total Absence, with One Caveat

Repair, in the relational sense, requires acknowledgment of harm caused, articulation of regret, behavior change credibly maintained, and tolerance of the wronged party's continued resentment during a reconstruction period. Helmut performs none of these steps in his ordinary range.

What he does instead, and only sometimes, is **renegotiate the contract.** With Moonstone, with Atlas, with various Thunderbolts who have variously betrayed and been betrayed by him, he is capable of returning to the table years later with a new proposition: *here is what I want, here is what you want, here is the structure by which both can be obtained.* He does not apologize. He does not concede that he was wrong. He simply offers terms that account for the prior breach by pricing it into the new arrangement. Some of his former victims accept, because the terms are honest in the narrow sense and because he is, when not in vendetta-mode, an unusually fair contractor.

**The caveat — the Ellis-era register.** In the late-2000s arcs, the subject demonstrates something that is *not* repair but is its nearest neighbor in his repertoire: **articulated ideological argument with former intimates that treats them as moral agents rather than as instruments.** He speaks to Songbird in this register; he speaks to Moonstone in this register. It is the closest thing in canon to him recognizing that he wronged people who had interior lives. He does not apologize even there. But he stops *managing* them and starts *addressing* them, and this is, for him, the maximal relational concession of which he has been shown capable.

---

## 4.7 Intimacy — What He Permits, What He Refuses

**Physical intimacy.** Documented liaisons across canon are sparse, transactional, and brief — primarily with Moonstone and one or two others, almost always in service of an operational alignment rather than as ends in themselves. There is no canonical evidence of him sustaining a sexual relationship past the point of its tactical utility. The body, for him, is an instrument like any other, and he is no more sentimental about his own than about others'. He is not ascetic — he eats well, dresses well, takes pleasure in the swordwork — but pleasure is curated, not sought, and never permitted to govern.

**Emotional intimacy.** Refused absolutely. No confidant has ever existed in his canonical life. He has no journal that has been recovered, no priest, no analyst he engages with honestly, no childhood friend retained into adulthood, no sibling. The mask is the perfect material symbol of this refusal: even his face is not given. To be intimate with Helmut Zemo is to be permitted a layer or two further into the curated outer presentation; the core, by deliberate construction, has no aperture.

**Self-intimacy.** Here the picture darkens. He does not appear to permit it of himself either. Across fifty years of canon, there are perhaps a half-dozen moments — the Born Better revelation, the late confrontation with the V-Battalion legacy, the quiet beat after he loses the Thunderbolts the first time — where he comes within reach of self-knowledge. He turns away from each one with discipline. The Heinrich question, in particular, he has the cognitive equipment to answer truthfully and **refuses to.** This refusal is the central act of his interior life. The hood covers the face; the discipline covers the question.

**Dependency.** He depends on no one operationally that he cannot replace. He depends on the *fact* of Captain America's existence in a way he would never name — the vendetta organizes him; without it, he is a man with a wardrobe and a sword and a worldview and no reason to get up. This is the dependency he cannot see and the one that costs him most. Rogers is, functionally, the load-bearing wall of Helmut Zemo's identity, and Helmut has spent fifty years trying to demolish the wall while standing on the floor it holds up.

---

## 4.8 The Repeated Relational Template

Every relationship Helmut Zemo forms across fifty years of canon follows, with minor variations of tempo and idiom, the same five-act structure. This is the diagnostic core of the section.

**Act I — Assessment.** Cold, swift, accurate. He determines the other party's capabilities, motivations, vulnerabilities, and price. The assessment is conducted under the cover of courtesy, often over a meal or in a formal setting where his etiquette does the work of disarming the subject. He typically completes it within the first sustained encounter. He is rarely wrong.

**Act II — Contract.** Explicit or tacit, the terms are established. He offers something the other party wants — resources, status, opportunity for vengeance, ideological belonging, the chance to be near greatness — and names, openly or by implication, what he requires in return. The contract is honored from his side with surprising punctilio for the duration of its utility. Subordinates often report, in this phase, that he is *the best commander they have served under.* This is true.

**Act III — Performance.** The relationship runs at peak effectiveness. He extracts maximum value; the other party often genuinely enjoys the work. The Thunderbolts, in the Citizen V phase, *loved being heroes.* The Masters of Evil, under his command, executed the most successful assault on the Avengers in their history. He is, when the contract is live, a deeply rewarding figure to work for and with, because his competence creates wins and his courtesy creates dignity. This is the seam that catches new partners every time.

**Act IV — Divergence.** The other party develops a desire that is not in the contract. They begin to want something he did not price in: to be loved by the public, to be morally legitimate, to be his equal rather than his subordinate, to be released, to be loved by him. He notices the divergence early. He does not address it. He recalculates.

**Act V — Termination.** By abandonment if the asset is reusable; by violence if the asset has become obstacle; by elaborate symbolic cruelty if the asset has wounded the Zemo name in the divergence. The terminations are clean from his interior accounting and devastating from the other party's. The other party — and this is the cruelest signature of the template — almost always reports, in the aftermath, that they *should have seen it coming.* He told them, in the contract, exactly what he was. They heard "I am Zemo" as a name. They were supposed to hear it as a warning.

This template runs with Heinrich's surviving loyalists, with the various Masters of Evil rosters, with each Thunderbolt by name, with Moonstone repeatedly, with the V-Battalion overture, with the modernized Winter Soldier handling, with every alliance he forms with other strategists (Osborn included), and — in inverted, mirrored form — **with Rogers himself, who is the only party who has ever exited the template at Act II by refusing the contract.** Rogers's refusal to be in any relationship with Zemo on Zemo's terms is the single fact Helmut cannot metabolize. It is why the vendetta will not end.

---

## 4.9 The Rogers Anomaly — Attachment Where Attachment Should Not Be

Every diagnostic above describes a man who does not form bonds. The Rogers cluster violates every term of that description and must be accounted for separately.

With Rogers, Helmut demonstrates: **intrusive cognition** (decades of unbidden return to the subject), **proximity-seeking** (he repeatedly engineers encounters that strategic logic would counsel against), **specificity of cruelty** (the Jarvis beating, the destruction of the Sarah Rogers photograph, the precise targeting of what Rogers *loves* rather than what Rogers *uses*), **inability to terminate** (no canonical decade has passed without a return), **affective decompensation in proximity** (his strategic IQ measurably drops within line of sight), and **a register of address — formal, intimate, ceremonial — that he uses with no one else.** These are, taxonomically, attachment behaviors. They are organized around hatred rather than love, but the **structure** is the structure of attachment.

The clinical reading: with no primary caregiver to occupy the attachment slot, and a named enemy installed in childhood with mythic intensity, the slot was filled by Rogers. The bond is real. The valence is inverted. The dependency is total and unacknowledged. He cannot leave Rogers alone because **leaving Rogers alone would leave Helmut Zemo alone with himself,** and the architecture of his interior does not support solo occupancy.

This is the relational fact under the relational facts: the only person he has ever truly attached to is the man he has spent his life trying to destroy, and the destruction has been deferred and deferred and deferred because, on a level he will not permit himself to know, **completion would be unsurvivable.** He will lose to Rogers as many times as it takes not to lose Rogers. The pattern of strategic-IQ collapse in Cap's presence is, read this way, **not a flaw in his planning. It is the planning working.**

---

## 4.10 Summary Diagnostic Card

- **Style:** Dismissive-avoidant, with arrested paternal idealization and a disorganized fragment exclusive to the Rogers cluster.
- **Capacity for bond:** Near zero, by training and by election; the one exception is structurally inverted (hatred occupying the attachment slot).
- **Mode of relation:** Contractual, hierarchical, performance-graded; relations are managed, not lived.
- **Distrust:** Calibrated rather than paranoid; baseline, not reactive; held without affect.
- **Betrayal (his):** Unaffected, ledger-clean, surprised by others' wounded reactions.
- **Betrayal (received):** Metabolized as confirmation; affect is contempt; the only intolerable form is being ideologically outperformed by a subordinate.
- **Repair:** Effectively absent; nearest neighbor is renegotiation on honest terms without apology; Ellis-era addresses-as-agents is the ceiling.
- **Intimacy:** Refused at every level — physical (transactional), emotional (impermissible), self- (disciplined-away).
- **Dependency:** Denied operationally, total in the unacknowledged Rogers attachment.
- **Template:** Assessment → Contract → Performance → Divergence → Termination, run identically against every party in his life across five decades, with Rogers as the lone party to refuse Act II and thereby remain.

The shape, restated for this section: a man trained from childhood not to need anyone, organized in adulthood around a relationship he cannot acknowledge as a relationship, performing courtesy as a containment field over a relational interior that contains, by careful construction, exactly one occupant — and that occupant is Captain America, installed by Heinrich Zemo in the year of Helmut's birth and never evicted since.

— END SECTION 4 —


## Defenses & Compensatory Mechanisms

# UATU DOSSIER — SUBJECT: HELMUT JULIUS FRITZ ZEMO
## Section 7: Defenses & Compensatory Mechanisms

---

### 7.0 Orienting Frame

The subject's defensive architecture is unusually **well-organized, hierarchically stratified, and ego-syntonic** — i.e., the defenses are not experienced by him as defenses but as virtues, methods, or simple facts of his nature. This is itself a diagnostic finding: the architecture has been load-bearing for so many decades, and so reliably, that he has built personality, vocation, and aesthetic on top of it. To strip the defenses would not produce a free man; it would produce rubble.

The architecture below is ranked from **most mature** (sublimatory, integrative, costly to install, durable under load) down to **most primitive** (splitting, identification with the aggressor, omnipotent control). The unusual feature of this subject is that he operates fluently at *both ends of the ladder* — he can deploy first-rate sublimation in the morning and naked identification with the aggressor by nightfall, with no apparent dissonance. Most personality structures cluster at a band on the ladder; his straddles. The straddle is the signature.

What follows is the field-operations manual to the man's interior.

---

### 7.1 The Mature Tier — Sublimation, Intellectualization, Anticipation, Humor

#### 7.1.1 Sublimation (heavy use, genuinely transformative)

Helmut converts immense quantities of aggressive and grief-laden affect into **disciplined cultural performance**: fencing, languages, history, tactical theory, the curation of objects, the etiquette of his own dress and address. The sublimation is not decorative. He *is* a master swordsman; he *does* read Clausewitz, Sun Tzu, Liddell Hart, the Augustan historians, the Frankfurt School (he reads his enemies' shelves), Carl Schmitt, von Moltke, and the Russian and French strategists in their original tongues. He plays out historical battles in solitary tabletop reconstruction. He spends real hours practicing épée forms with no one watching. These activities do not exist to display competence — they exist to **bind the aggressive drive into a form that can be exhibited without shame.**

Operationally observable signatures of sublimation:
- He arrives early to operations and walks the ground; the walking is contemplative, not surveillant.
- Long-form reading occupies the dead time most operatives fill with stimulation.
- He composes, in private, written analyses of his own past defeats — these documents are recovered in safe-house seizures and read like a general's after-action reports, not like a wounded man's diary. *That distinction is the sublimation working.*

The cost: sublimation requires that the underlying affect be **converted, not addressed.** Helmut has spent fifty years converting grief over his father into operational excellence and has therefore never had the grief. The reservoir does not drain; it gets repurposed. When sublimation fails (Cap in the room), the unconverted affect surfaces at full original pressure — see §7.4 below.

#### 7.1.2 Intellectualization (primary, ego-syntonic, ubiquitous)

The dominant defense. Every wound becomes a problem. Every problem becomes a chart, a campaign, a counterfactual. The father's death is not a grief; it is a *case study.* The Adhesive X disfigurement is not a body-horror; it is a *datum about polymer chemistry to be later monetized in operations.* Songbird's defection is not a betrayal; it is *a variable I underweighted.*

The hallmark of his intellectualization is **the substitution of taxonomies for feelings.** Where a less defended man would say *I am angry,* Helmut says *Rogers represents the third category of opposing actor — the morally legible adversary whose virtue functions as armor.* The proposition is true. It is also the place where the anger went.

Behavioral microsignals:
- Speech rate slows under emotional pressure; vocabulary becomes more precise, more Latinate, more clausal.
- He answers questions about feelings with statements about systems.
- In interrogation transcripts he routinely reframes the interrogator's question into a more interesting question and answers that one. Clinicians log this as evasion; it is in fact the defense operating in real time.

#### 7.1.3 Anticipation (well-developed)

He pre-suffers losses. He runs the failure case in detail before committing. This is why he survives so many catastrophes: he has already, in imagination, lost the Mansion, lost the Thunderbolts, lost the face, lost the war. The arrival of the loss is therefore not shattering but **recognizable, even familiar.** When he goes underground after the Osborn displacement, the move is not improvised — he had pre-fitted the bolt-hole and the new identity months earlier. Anticipation is what allows him to *fall gracefully.*

The cost: anticipation taken too far becomes a kind of pre-mourning that drains commitment. He is occasionally **insufficiently invested in his own victory** because he has already rehearsed losing it. This shows up in the rooftop fights — once the strategic plan slips, he transitions into a kind of theatrical loss-acceptance rather than scrambling for a tactical recovery.

#### 7.1.4 Humor (dry, controlled, mature)

A genuinely funny man within a narrow band. The humor is **arid, observational, often at his own expense**, and almost always at the expense of others' pretensions to virtue. He finds heroes faintly ridiculous and says so in epigrams. He laughs at his own most pompous moments in retrospect. The humor is a mature defense because it does **acknowledge** the absurdity it disarms — it does not deny.

Diagnostic note: the humor disappears in Rogers's presence. A man who can joke about his own father's permanent face-mask becomes, in front of Captain America, **completely unable to find the situation funny.** The unfunny-Cap-zone is among the most reliable signals in his entire behavioral repertoire.

---

### 7.2 The Neurotic Tier — Reaction Formation, Isolation of Affect, Rationalization, Displacement

#### 7.2.1 Reaction Formation (massive, specifically around the father)

The single most overdetermined defense in the file. Heinrich was a Nazi; Helmut adopts **Citizen V**, his anti-Nazi grandfather's identity, as his most ambitious and prolonged mask. The choice is presented internally as cynical instrumentation — *the public will trust this symbol* — but the persistence, the **fidelity** with which he plays the role (saving civilians, making correct moral calls, *being a competent hero for months*), exceeds what cynicism requires. The role-fidelity is the giveaway.

What is being defended against is the unacknowledgeable knowledge that **the father was contemptible.** Helmut cannot let himself know this directly without the lineage frame collapsing and his life becoming retrospectively absurd. So he installs the antithesis as a costume, lets himself live inside it, and then — crucially — has to **destroy the costume from within** by revealing the deception. The reveal is necessary because to let Citizen V continue would be to admit Citizen V was preferable.

Other reaction-formation traces:
- Extreme courtesy toward subordinates whose loyalty he is about to spend.
- Insistence on personal honor with peers he is currently betraying strategically.
- Aesthetic asceticism in private (austere quarters, monastic schedule) inside operations of baroque cruelty.

#### 7.2.2 Isolation of Affect (constant, near-perfect)

He can describe his father's death, his own disfigurement, the loss of the Thunderbolts, and the killing of subordinates in the **same tonal register** — measured, accurate, faintly amused. The content and the affect are surgically separated. Clinicians who have evaluated him in custody report leaving the session feeling *they* are the unsettled party; the patient appears regulated to a degree that itself becomes unsettling. This is not flat affect (which would be alexithymic). It is **active, ongoing dissection** of feeling from narrative, performed continuously and with skill.

#### 7.2.3 Rationalization (sophisticated, philosophically literate)

Rationalization in him is unusually high-grade. He does not produce post-hoc excuses; he produces **post-hoc political philosophies.** The world-conquest plans come pre-wrapped in coherent (if abhorrent) doctrine — order versus chaos, the unfitness of the mass for self-government, the cowardice of refusing the rulership one's competence implies. Schmitt, Nietzsche-filtered-through-aristocracy, a sprinkling of de Maistre. The doctrine is sincere as performance and tactical as function: it makes vengeance look like statesmanship.

The signature of rationalization as a *defense* (rather than as a conviction) is that the doctrine **adjusts to fit the operation**, never the reverse. When the operation requires posing as a hero, he discovers heroic doctrine. When it requires authoritarian conquest, he discovers authoritarian doctrine. The flexibility is the defense; the conviction is the wallpaper.

#### 7.2.4 Displacement (focused, almost ritualized)

The vast underlying rage at **the father who died and left him a feud instead of a parent** cannot be discharged at its true object. It is displaced onto Rogers — the agent of the father's death — and is then perpetually re-displaced onto Rogers's intimates and symbols: Bucky, Jarvis, Sarah Rogers's photograph, the Captain America costume itself when worn by surrogates. The Mansion sequence (Avengers #273–277) is a textbook displacement cascade: he cannot reach the father; he reaches the man who killed the father; failing to settle that, he attacks the *butler who loves the man who killed the father.* The further from the original object, the more cruelly the displaced affect lands — because the further surrogate cannot absorb it meaningfully, only suffer it.

---

### 7.3 The Borderline Tier — Splitting (Tactical), Devaluation, Idealization

#### 7.3.1 Splitting — *unusual variant: cognitively tactical, not perceptually compulsive*

He splits, but he splits **with his eyes open.** Most splitters cannot see the good in the all-bad object; Helmut can enumerate Cap's virtues with the precision of a hagiographer and *hates him for them.* The split is therefore not perceptual failure but **affective categorization** — Rogers is placed in the bin marked *to be destroyed* and then all subsequent data, including admiring data, gets filed without changing the bin. This is a more dangerous form of splitting than the classical borderline variant, because it is immune to the corrective effect of evidence.

The same applies in reverse to the father. Heinrich is in the bin marked *to be honored*, and unflattering data about Heinrich (his cruelty, his collaboration, his ridiculous mask-mishap) gets filed without changing the bin. The Born Better arc is the only documented moment where the bin assignment **wavers** — and the wavering is immediately re-stabilized by Helmut's decision to position himself as the *improved* Zemo, which preserves the lineage frame.

#### 7.3.2 Devaluation (constant, low-affect)

He devalues continuously and almost without effort. Subordinates are tools; allies are temporary; the public is a mass; democracies are sentimentalities; heroes are children. The devaluation is not contemptuous in tone — it is **clerical**, a matter of correct classification. This makes it more durable than ordinary contempt because it does not require energy to maintain.

#### 7.3.3 Idealization — *narrow but deep*

Reserved almost entirely for the father, the lineage, the title, and (in inverted form) the enemy. The idealization of Heinrich is the structural keystone; remove it and the whole architecture loses its load path. This is why he cannot afford to examine the father directly. The idealization is what the rest of the building rests on.

---

### 7.4 The Primitive Tier — Identification with the Aggressor, Omnipotent Control, Projective Identification

#### 7.4.1 Identification with the Aggressor (the deepest single fact)

He became **what disfigured his father** rather than **what his father was.** The father was an unmasked scientist; the agent of his fate was the masked, scarred figure (and the chemical that produced one). Helmut, having tried to inflict the father's fate on Rogers and inflicted it instead on himself, **completed the identification** in the very act of attempting vengeance. The hood is the identification made wearable.

This is why the mask cannot be removed. It is not vanity, not trauma-aversion, not even brand — those are surface accounts. It is that **the mask is who he became when he tried to be his father's avenger and discovered he had become his father's killer's instrument.** To uncover the face is to confront the fusion. He will not.

Behavioral consequences:
- He fights with the weapons of his enemies (Avengers tactics, Cap's own playbook) more readily than with his father's tools (chemistry, lab-craft). Heinrich's methods bore him; Cap's methods seduce him.
- He has, across decades, **gotten better at being like Cap than at being like Heinrich** — better at command presence, better at moral framing, better at leading men through hardship.
- The Citizen V deception works partly because Cap-identification gives him real material to draw on.

#### 7.4.2 Omnipotent Control (chronic, partially reality-tested)

He believes, accurately within limits and inaccurately past them, that **sufficient intellect plus sufficient preparation can determine outcomes.** The belief is rewarded often enough to be reinforced and disconfirmed rarely enough to remain stable. When the disconfirmations come (the Thunderbolts, the Mansion roof, Osborn's takeover), they are absorbed via anticipation (§7.1.3) and intellectualization (§7.1.2) rather than producing humility.

The defense shows up operationally as:
- Over-planning to the point of brittleness — contingency trees so dense that any unmodeled variable becomes catastrophic.
- A characteristic **refusal to delegate the symbolic moment** — he will execute the climactic act personally because the act must register on the universe through *his* hand.
- A genuine difficulty believing that subordinates have interior lives that will produce unmodeled wants. The Thunderbolts collapse is omnipotent control meeting its limit and not understanding what it has met.

#### 7.4.3 Projective Identification (active, weaponized)

He places into others the affect he refuses to feel and then **operates on them as if it were theirs.** He provokes rage in Rogers and reads it as evidence of Rogers's barbarity. He provokes desperation in Songbird and reads it as evidence of her instability. He provokes grief in himself by destroying Jarvis in front of Cap, *and feels Cap's grief as the satisfying object* — i.e., his own grief, externalized, witnessed, and used as fuel. This is among the most primitive defenses he employs and one of the most reliable.

#### 7.4.4 Turning Against the Self (rare but spectacular)

The Adhesive X immersion is the type-case. Under conditions of overwhelming patrilineal affect, he literalizes the wound on his own body — taking the father's fate into himself. This is a defense of last resort and he has used it only a handful of times across canon, but each instance is irreversible. The face is permanent. The lineage choices are permanent. When he turns against himself, he does it once and finally.

---

### 7.5 Compensatory Mechanisms — Positive Constellation

These are the *load-bearing virtues* that the defensive architecture produces as byproducts. They are not insincere; they are real capacities that the defenses required him to develop.

- **Genuine erudition.** Languages (German, English, French, Russian to native fluency; functional Italian, Latin, classical Greek; technical Japanese; some Sokovian dialect material). Reading across military history, political philosophy, chemistry, comparative religion, art history. The erudition is the residue of decades of intellectualization that had to find subject matter.
- **Master-level swordsmanship.** Épée and saber to competition standard, plus traditional sabre forms and rapier work for ritual occasions. Daily practice. The sword is not a weapon of operational choice; it is a **mnemonic for discipline** — the practice maintains the defensive architecture's tonus.
- **Eidetic or near-eidetic recall.** Functions as both cognitive capacity and defense — he never has to *re-feel* a memory because he can re-access it as data.
- **Contract reliability.** Within narrowly specified agreements, his word is good. Honor as personal code (not moral law) is a compensatory virtue with operational utility — peers will deal with him because he keeps deals.
- **Capacity for command.** Real, tested, repeatedly demonstrated. He leads competently under fire, allocates correctly, takes responsibility for losses in after-action.
- **Aesthetic taste.** Genuine, conservative, austere. Curates objects for meaning, not display. His safe-houses are recognizable by the shared sensibility — Bauhaus over Rococo, a small good library over a large vulgar one.
- **Physical discipline.** Peak human conditioning maintained into late middle age via régime: morning forms, evening reading, no pharmacological dependency, controlled diet, ceremonial alcohol only. The body is treated as another instrument the mind owns.
- **Tactical empathy.** The capacity to model what others will *do* (distinct from what they will want) is extraordinarily well-developed and serves him in every operation.

#### Negative Constellation

These are the costs the architecture imposes — the maladaptive byproducts that recur reliably and that he has not, across fifty years, learned to interrupt.

- **The hood as compulsion.** It cannot come off in public, in private, in mirrors. The wound beneath is small; the meaning beneath is total.
- **The Cap fixation.** A drive that has cost him every long-game victory he was within reach of. He cannot extract value from a hostage Rogers without first wounding Rogers, and the wounding always costs the extraction.
- **The sadism in vendetta-mode.** Strategically valueless, reliably present, repeatedly catastrophic. The Jarvis beating is the clean instance: the only thing that operation needed was *not to do that,* and he could not not do it.
- **The inability to walk away from a humiliation.** He returns to former teammates who defeated him, to facilities that beat him, to symbols that mocked him. Each return is a degradation of his strategic posture and he makes them anyway.
- **The intolerance of being ideologically out-performed by a subordinate.** Songbird being a better hero than Citizen V was *as a performance* was, for him, more annihilating than the operational failure of the deception itself.
- **The lineage trap.** All available self-moves are *better Zemo* or *worse Zemo,* never *not Zemo.* This forecloses entire categories of life he is otherwise equipped to live.
- **Boredom intolerance.** Under-recognized in most assessments. A Helmut Zemo with nothing operationally interesting to do invents cruelty as cognitive entertainment. The architecture requires problems to metabolize; absent problems, it generates them.
- **The unfunny zone around Cap.** A reliable indicator that the defenses have offlined and the primitive tier is in command. When humor disappears, omnipotent control and identification with the aggressor are running the room.
- **Symbolic acting-out under stress.** The mimetic Adhesive X choice, the destruction of Sarah Rogers's photographs, the staging of the Jarvis beating *in front of* Cap — every one of these is a strategic error performed because the symbol demanded it. The architecture cannot route around symbol once symbol enters the field.

---

### 7.6 The Hierarchy in Operation — A Cascade Under Load

The decisive observation is that the defenses **cascade in a predictable sequence under increasing pressure**, and the cascade has been the same across every documented decompensation in the canon.

**Baseline (no Cap, no lineage threat):** Sublimation, intellectualization, anticipation, humor. He is the courteous strategist, the cultured aristocrat, the competent commander. The mature tier is in charge and he is *good company* by his own lights.

**Low stress (operational complications, ordinary opposition):** Reaction formation activates around any moral framing, rationalization produces doctrine on demand, isolation of affect handles losses. The neurotic tier is in charge and he is **at his most dangerous** — the planning is sharpest, the doctrine most persuasive, the affect most absent.

**Moderate stress (Cap in proximity, lineage invoked):** Splitting becomes louder, devaluation more open, displacement begins to escalate against surrogates. The borderline tier comes online; the operation begins to drift from objective toward symbol.

**High stress (Cap engaged, name at stake):** Identification with the aggressor and omnipotent control take over. Projective identification weaponizes itself in the climactic act. He stages something that has no operational point and serves only to discharge the unmetabolizable affect through the body of a surrogate.

**Catastrophic stress (the wound itself touched):** Turning against the self — rare, irreversible, foundational. The Adhesive X moment is the type-case and the originating one.

The cascade has run, with variations, in 1973, in 1986, in the closing arcs of the original Thunderbolts run, in the Liberators sequence, in the post-Osborn period, in the Bucky-vendetta material. **He has never broken the cascade.** Each time, the mature tier holds longer than the time before; each time, the cascade still completes. The mind is improving its top stories and rebuilding nothing in the basement.

---

### 7.7 Operational Implications

For any party seeking to **engage** the subject productively:
- Engage at the mature tier. He is approachable, even congenial, in the register of strategy, history, aesthetics, and contract. He keeps deals struck in that register.
- Do not invoke the father, the lineage, the Citizen V theft, or Rogers unless the goal is to *destabilize* him — these invocations are reliable but they are one-way doors. He will not forgive having been read.

For any party seeking to **defeat** the subject:
- Run the cascade. Put Cap (or the Cap-symbol) in the room. The strategic IQ drops measurably. The symbolic acting-out follows. The catastrophic tactical error follows that. The architecture defeats itself if pressed at the correct point.
- Do not let him stabilize at the mature tier with time to plan. Time is his medium; deny it.

For any party seeking to **understand** the subject (this office's brief):
- The defenses are the man. There is no concealed authentic self beneath them waiting to be liberated. The architecture is the architecture *of* the self. The face beneath the hood is not the true Zemo; the hood is. The man who took the mask off would not be the real Helmut revealed — he would be a different person entirely, and that person has never existed and will not be permitted to.

The hood is the answer to every question this section poses. He covered the wound and built a life on the covering. The covering became the life. To assess Helmut Zemo's defenses is to assess Helmut Zemo, because in his case those are the same object, examined from two sides.

— END SECTION 7 —


## Longitudinal Psychological Profile

# LONGITUDINAL PSYCHOLOGICAL PROFILE — HELMUT JULIUS FRITZ ZEMO

## Subject File §4 / Decadal Clinical Mapping

A clinical picture rendered across the subject's documented life is not a single portrait but a series of strata — each decade a sedimentary layer in which the same underlying structure (avoidant attachment, narcissistic organization, obsessional fixation, identification with a disfigured father) is expressed through a different surface vocabulary. What follows is the decade-by-decade mapping of affect regulation, cognitive style, and self-concept, with each stratum read against its predecessor to isolate true evolution from mere costume-change.

---

### I. PRE-DEBUT: CHILDHOOD AND ADOLESCENCE (roughly the 1950s–60s in the original timeline; modernized to the 1980s–90s on the Sokovian/Carpathian estate)

**Affect regulation.** Reconstructable only by inference, but the inference is strong. A child raised inside a household whose central organizing fact is the absent father's mutilation and death cannot develop ordinary affect-tolerance. The available models are two: the dead idealized parent (silent, perfect, unreachable) and the staff/tutors (subordinated, formal, instrumentally responsive). Neither model teaches a child what to do with grief, fear, or shame. The expected adaptation — which the adult subject displays in textbook form — is *containment by stylization*: feeling is converted at the threshold of awareness into something else, usually a posture, a phrase, or a plan. By adolescence the subject has almost certainly internalized the household register: emotion is vulgar; bearing is everything; the Zemo who weeps has surrendered.

**Cognitive style.** High native endowment (later evidenced by polyglossia to native fluency in four languages, near-eidetic recall, master-level fencing pedagogy absorbed before adulthood) channelled into the curriculum a disgraced aristocratic house provides: classics, military history, chemistry (the patrimony), languages, the sword. This is not a *creative* education; it is a *consolidating* one. The young subject is taught to map, to memorize, to systematize — not to invent. The signature adult cognitive habit of long-horizon plan-construction with weak modeling of others' *desires* (as opposed to behavior) is laid down here: he is trained to predict moves on a board, not motives in a heart.

**Self-concept.** The child does not develop a self in the ordinary sense; he develops a *position* — heir, last of the line, sole vessel for a wronged name. The Eriksonian failure is in autonomy and initiative: he is never permitted to be merely a person, only an inheritor. This produces in adulthood the characteristic inability to conceive of *not being a Zemo* as a live option. The Born Better arc, decades later, will reveal this lock with perfect clarity — confronted with proof that his entire line was monstrous, he can only imagine being a *better* Zemo, never a *former* one. That foreclosure is installed in the nursery.

---

### II. THE PHOENIX ERA — EARLY ADULTHOOD, FIRST EMERGENCE (Captain America #168, 1973; the months before, during, and immediately after the Adhesive X immersion)

**Affect regulation.** Catastrophically poor under his one chosen stressor, undetectably ordinary under all others. The Phoenix operation reveals a young man whose composure holds through reconnaissance, infiltration, and capture — and dissolves at the moment of consummation, when the option of merely killing Rogers is rejected in favor of the symbolically perfect kill (Adhesive X, the father's compound, the father's wound replicated on the father's killer). This is the diagnostic event of the file. **Affect regulation is intact for instrumental action and absent for symbolic action.** The fall into the vat is not bad luck; it is the predictable consequence of attempting to perform ritual in an operational moment. The adult subject will repeat this exact failure mode, against the same target, for the next fifty years.

**Cognitive style.** Already long-horizon, already meticulous, but at this stage *uniformly* in service of vengeance. There is no separable ideological project yet — the worldview that will later justify world-conquest is still entirely subordinated to the personal vendetta. Counterfactual reasoning is present (he has built a plan that anticipates Rogers's defenses); strategic creativity is present (the Phoenix alias as misdirection); but **the higher-order capacity to ask whether the plan itself is the right plan is absent.** He cannot, in 1973, step outside his own grievance to audit it.

**Self-concept.** Fused with the father. The Phoenix alias is itself revealing: a creature reborn from its own ashes, but the ashes are not the subject's — they are Heinrich's. He is reborn *as his father,* not as himself. The Adhesive X event then completes the identification literally: he leaves the vat wearing his father's wound. The hood is donned within days. From this point forward, every public appearance of the subject is an unbroken act of carrying his father's disfigurement on his own face. **This is the most overdetermined symptom in the file.** Identification with the aggressor, mimetic introjection of the lost object, and reaction-formation against the visible truth of his own ruined face all converge in a single piece of purple cloth.

---

### III. THE LONG INTERREGNUM AND THE MASTERS OF EVIL (mid-1970s through 1986, culminating in *Under Siege*, Avengers #270–277)

**Affect regulation.** Substantial improvement at baseline; the same catastrophic decompensation at the target. During the years of preparation he is, by all observable measures, a functioning master tactician — recruiting, training, financing, and coordinating the largest super-criminal coalition in canonical history. He runs Wrecking Crew thugs and Absorbing Man alongside Tiger Shark and the Fixer without the roster fragmenting, which requires a level of interpersonal calibration that argues for *much* better affect-regulation than the Phoenix-era subject possessed. He has learned to wait.

What he has not learned is what to do once the waiting is over. The Mansion sequence is the second clean instance of his signature pathology: a flawless operational achievement (Avengers captured, base seized, Jarvis taken hostage) followed by a strategically valueless symbolic indulgence (Jarvis beaten in front of Rogers, Sarah Rogers's photographs destroyed, the Bucky materials desecrated). **Every minute spent on the symbolic act is a minute Rogers is gathering himself.** The subject knows this and cannot stop. The rooftop fall ensues.

The escalation ladder is now visible as a stable pattern across two iterations: *strategic execution → symbolic flourish → personal cruelty → catastrophic tactical error.* By 1986 this is no longer a youthful error; it is a structural feature of the subject's psychology under the Cap stimulus.

**Cognitive style.** Maturation evident. He now plans in multi-actor systems rather than single-vector vendettas. He shows the first signs of ideological articulation — the Masters of Evil are described in his internal monologue and in his speeches to the team as a *corrective* to a world that has surrendered to costumed sentimentality. The vengeance is still primary but a doctrine is beginning to crystallize around it. He has also begun to demonstrate the durable strength that will define him for the next forty years: he reads people behaviorally with great precision (he correctly anticipates Cap's tactical decisions, the Wasp's hesitation, Hercules's berserk overreach), while reading them motivationally with persistent error (he does not foresee that Jarvis's endurance will *strengthen* Cap rather than break him).

**Self-concept.** Hardening into the form it will hold for life. He is now consciously the inheritor of a *project,* not just a feud. The aristocratic-exceptional self-image is fully online: he refers to his confederates as instruments; he addresses Rogers as a man who deserves to lose to him specifically. The wound beneath the hood has been re-narrated from accident to fate: he carries Heinrich's mark because he is Heinrich's continuation. The repudiation of this self-concept will not occur in any decade of his subsequent life.

---

### IV. THE CITIZEN V / THUNDERBOLTS DECEPTION (1996–1999, *Thunderbolts* #1–25 and contemporaneous tie-ins)

**Affect regulation.** The high-water mark of his life. To run the Thunderbolts deception he must, every day, for months, perform a personality he despises in front of cameras, civilians, government liaisons, and his own teammates — never breaking, never gloating, never sneering. He does it. The man who could not resist beating a butler in 1986 disciplines himself in 1997 to deliver an unbroken impersonation of a public servant. This is not a different person; it is the same person discovering that *strategy* can hold against the symbolic urge when the strategic prize is large enough. The Citizen V era proves that the decompensation pattern is contingent rather than inevitable — *given a sufficiently grandiose goal, the obsessional indulgences can be suppressed.* The implication is sobering: he could, in principle, regulate himself indefinitely. He chooses not to whenever the stakes drop below world-historical.

**Cognitive style.** Peak. The Thunderbolts deception is the most cognitively impressive operation he ever runs: it requires modeling an entire grieving public, anticipating institutional responses (S.H.I.E.L.D., the press, the surviving heroic community), choreographing six superhuman careers in parallel, and maintaining narrative consistency across improvised emergencies. He inhabits a perspective he holds in contempt — a frightened civilian wanting to be saved — and gives that perspective exactly what it wants. This is the operation of a first-rate theory-of-mind under sustained adversarial conditions.

The single, decisive cognitive failure is the one the workup correctly isolates: **he models behavior brilliantly and motivation poorly.** He predicts what his teammates will *do* in any given crisis; he does not predict what they will come to *want* after months of being loved by strangers. The Songbird/MACH/Atlas defection is not a tactical surprise; it is a *motivational* surprise. He had not represented in his planning the possibility that an identity, worn long enough, becomes a desire. This is a deep flaw in his cognition that persists for the rest of his life — he is a behaviorist in a world of agents.

**Self-concept.** Splits, briefly and instructively. For the duration of the deception the subject must hold two self-images simultaneously: Citizen V the public servant and Helmut Zemo the puppet-master. Most narcissistic structures cannot do this without leakage; his does. The implication is that the *performance* of virtue costs him nothing because virtue is, in his ontology, just another set of behaviors. He does not experience hypocrisy because he does not experience the public self as a self at all. This is diagnostically important: he is not a man pretending to be good and feeling shame about it; he is a man pretending to be good with the same affective register he would bring to pretending to be a Frenchman.

The collapse, when it comes, is also self-concept revealing. He is not undone by enemies; he is undone by his own subordinates' *aspiration.* The wound is narcissistic in the technical sense — the people he was using have shown him they are capable of something he is not (sincere desire to be better), and the show of their capacity is intolerable. He responds with the predictable vengeance arc.

---

### V. THE EXILE AND THE LIBERATORS PERIOD (late 1990s through mid-2000s, *Thunderbolts* #25–75, *Citizen V & the V-Battalion* tie-ins)

**Affect regulation.** Degrades from the Citizen V peak but does not return to pre-1986 baseline. The exile arcs show a man who absorbs being deposed by Moonstone, rejected by the V-Battalion, and humiliated by his own former team without the kind of immediate symbolic acting-out that characterized the Phoenix era. He plots, he waits, he returns. The waiting is longer and quieter than before. What surfaces in this period for the first time is something that resembles *resignation* — not depression, but a settled tolerance for setbacks. He has begun, possibly without recognizing it, to accept that the Cap vendetta and the world-order project are now competing goals rather than the same goal.

**Cognitive style.** Branches into two distinct operational modes that will alternate for the rest of his career. **Mode A:** the world-historical ideologue, designing global empowerment schemes (the Liberators arc, the energy redistribution plans), thinking at planetary scale and decadal horizon. **Mode B:** the personal avenger, running surgical vendettas against specific former associates. The two modes coexist uncomfortably; the subject does not appear able to integrate them. When he is in Mode A he is at his most cognitively impressive and least emotionally regulated *toward the project's broad goals*; when he is in Mode B he is at his most affectively engaged and least strategically efficient. The alternation is itself the diagnostic feature: he has not become two people, but he has stopped being able to do both jobs at once.

**Self-concept.** First articulation of the full authoritarian doctrine in his own voice. He says, repeatedly, across multiple writers' runs, that he does not believe ordinary humans capable of self-governance and regards heroes as competent people humiliated into taking orders from the median voter. This is not a defensive screen for the vendetta; the consistency across writers indicates a genuine ideological commitment. **The self-concept in this period adds a layer:** he is no longer *only* the heir of a wronged house. He is now also the *philosopher* of an unmade order. The grandiosity has acquired content. This is, paradoxically, a stabilizing development — a narcissistic structure with a real doctrine is less brittle than one organized purely around an injury.

---

### VI. THE ELLIS-ERA AUSTERITY (mid-to-late 2000s, *Thunderbolts* #110 onward, *Civil War* peripheries)

**Affect regulation.** Pronounced improvement. This is the period in which observers begin to describe the subject as *world-weary* rather than enraged. He converses with Moonstone and Songbird in registers of philosophical disagreement rather than betrayal-vengeance. He concedes ground he would once have fought for. He recognizes Norman Osborn as more unstable than himself — a correct assessment requiring real self-knowledge, since it requires him to acknowledge that his own grandiosity is bounded by realism in a way Osborn's is not — and he withdraws rather than contest the field. The Mode A / Mode B alternation softens; for a sustained period the ideological frame dominates and the personal-vendetta tics recede.

Two readings are possible and probably both true. First, sheer cumulative learning: forty years of losing has taught him something about which fights pay. Second, a quasi-depressive *narcissistic deflation* — the realization that the world contains other and worse narcissists than himself, that his project will not be unique, that he may have peaked. The Ellis-era flatness has the affective texture of a man who has stopped expecting to win and has not yet decided what to do with that.

**Cognitive style.** Reflective in a way he has not been before. He is, in this period, the most credibly *intellectual* version of himself — not just clever but contemplative. He acknowledges arguments against his position without immediately needing to defeat them. The capacity for genuine ideological argument (rather than rationalized vengeance) is most evident here. This is also the period in which his strategic patience reaches its widest horizon: he is willing to be displaced for years if displacement serves the long arc.

**Self-concept.** Subtly recalibrated. For the first time in canon, the subject seems to entertain — without endorsing — the possibility that he is *a* man rather than *the* Zemo. The recalibration does not last and does not reach the level of admitted insight, but it is detectable in his willingness to walk away from contested ground and in the philosophical register of his confrontations. It is the closest he ever comes to a developmental transition. He does not cross it.

---

### VII. THE *BORN BETTER* THRESHOLD (late 2000s, the time-travel arc through the Zemo bloodline)

**Affect regulation.** Stable but tested. To trace his lineage back through medieval Europe and discover his ancestors uniformly monstrous is the kind of revelation that classically produces narcissistic collapse — the idealized lineage exposed as a pageant of cruelty. The subject does not collapse. He metabolizes the discovery within the existing structure, which is itself diagnostically vivid: even truth this large cannot escape the lineage frame.

**Cognitive style.** The arc demonstrates the cognitive ceiling and floor of the subject in a single move. The *ceiling*: he is genuinely curious, undertakes the genealogical investigation seriously, accepts the findings, and refuses to lie to himself about them. The *floor*: presented with an obvious exit from the lineage prison (the data say his bloodline is rotten; the rational move is to step out of the lineage frame), he does not see the exit. The only conceivable response, within his ontology, is to redefine the family mission. *Not Zemo* remains unthinkable; *better Zemo* is the only move.

**Self-concept.** The most important sentence in the dossier is the subject's own, in this arc: he is, for the first time, *better than his father.* This is the first admission across forty years that Heinrich was wrong about anything. It is also the first move that establishes a self-concept *separable* from Heinrich, even by a millimeter. The reaction-formation that produced the Citizen V alias decades earlier has finally surfaced in the subject's own voice: he can now state, to himself, that the father was not a great man and that the son must therefore be a different kind of Zemo. **This is the closest thing to therapeutic insight in the entire record.** It is not insight into his pathology; it is insight into his father. The two are not the same, but they are adjacent. He never bridges the remaining gap.

---

### VIII. THE MODERN OSCILLATION (2010s onward — Brubaker/Spencer/Zub Cap-and-Bucky arcs and their successors)

**Affect regulation.** Bimodal and unstable. When the subject is operating at distance from Rogers and the Bucky-symbol — running schemes against governments, manipulating intelligence services, conducting his ideological project at scale — he displays the Ellis-era calm and the Citizen V-era discipline in combination, and is, by some distance, the most capable version of himself ever seen. When Rogers or Bucky enters the operational field, the regulation collapses back to the Mansion-era pattern within minutes. **The escalation ladder is unchanged after fifty years.** Strategic execution, symbolic flourish, personal cruelty, catastrophic tactical error — the sequence still runs. The weaponization of Bucky's trigger-word conditioning is the cleanest modern instance: a brilliant operational coup converted, almost compulsively, into an intimate humiliation aimed at Rogers, which then exposes him.

The most parsimonious clinical reading is that the Cap/Bucky stimulus reliably triggers a *state-shift* in the subject — from a high-functioning narcissistic-ideologue baseline to a regressed vendetta state that resembles the early Phoenix-era subject almost line for line. The state-shift is not under voluntary control. Fifty years of repetition without modification argues that it is not capable of being brought under control by any means available to the subject himself.

**Cognitive style.** At baseline, the most sophisticated it has ever been. He now thinks across intelligence-agency timelines, manipulates multiple governments, and runs information operations of considerable subtlety. He is also more *patient* than at any prior point — willing to lose individual engagements for years to position a single later move. The behavior-vs-motivation modeling gap remains: he still loses to opponents who develop wants he did not foresee. This is a stable cognitive signature across the entire life.

**Self-concept.** Crystallized. The hood, once a wound-management object, is now openly described in the subject's own voice as *brand and ritual.* The face beneath is no longer the point; the iconography is. He has become, in the technical sense, his own monument — a man whose self-concept is now mediated through his own legend rather than through any continuing developmental process. This is the terminal form of the narcissistic structure: the self has been so thoroughly converted into image that the original psychological material is no longer accessible to the subject. He could not, at this point, locate the boy on the Bavarian/Sokovian estate even if he tried. He does not try.

---

### IX. CROSS-DECADAL SYNTHESIS — WHAT EVOLVED, WHAT DID NOT

**What evolved.**
- *Affect regulation at baseline:* from catastrophic (Phoenix era) to excellent (Ellis era and after), with the Citizen V period as the proof-of-concept that the subject can in principle hold himself indefinitely when sufficiently motivated.
- *Ideological articulation:* from raw vengeance with no doctrine (1973) to a fully developed authoritarian philosophy (mid-2000s onward) with internally consistent commitments that survive across writers.
- *Strategic horizon:* from months (Phoenix) to years (Masters of Evil) to decades (Citizen V deception and after).
- *Tolerance for setback:* dramatically improved. The young subject could not absorb a defeat without immediate symbolic counter-action; the mature subject can absorb a decade of displacement.
- *Self-concept content:* from inheritor-of-grievance to philosopher-of-order to self-as-iconography. Each shift adds rather than replaces.
- *Knowledge of self:* one true gain, in *Born Better* — the admission that the father was not great. Never extended into a knowledge of his own pathology.

**What did not evolve.**
- *The Cap/Bucky state-shift.* Unchanged for fifty years. The single most robust pathological pattern in the file.
- *The behavior-vs-motivation modeling gap.* He still loses to opponents whose desires he did not foresee. This is now best understood as a structural cognitive feature, not a correctable error.
- *The lineage foreclosure.* *Not Zemo* remains unthinkable. Every revision of self-concept occurs within the frame the nursery installed.
- *The absence of peer attachment.* No durable bond across the entire record. The dismissive-avoidant template is intact.
- *The conversion of intimate injury into operational catastrophe.* The escalation ladder runs identically in 1973 and in the modern era. He has learned much; he has not learned this.
- *The hood.* Function evolves (wound → brand) but presence does not. The face is never voluntarily uncovered in the presence of an enemy across the entire record.

**Clinical bottom line.** The subject is one of the most cognitively impressive personalities the file system has ever documented and one of the most stably pathological. His evolution is real but bounded: he has become a better tactician, a more articulate ideologue, a more patient operator, and — once, briefly, in *Born Better* — a slightly more honest son. He has not become a different man. The narcissistic structure has absorbed every developmental opportunity presented to it and re-expressed each as a refinement of the same self. He is now, in his maturity, exactly what the developmental ecology predicted: a first-rate mind organized around a wound he treats as a mandate, wearing his father's disfigurement as his own face, capable of nearly anything except the one move — letting an injury go unanswered — that would allow him to stop being a Zemo for a single afternoon.

— END §4


## Psychiatric Assessment & Differential

# PSYCHIATRIC ASSESSMENT & DIFFERENTIAL
## Subject: Helmut Julius Fritz Zemo (Baron Zemo, 13th of the name)
### File Section 04 — Forensic Psychiatric Formulation

---

## 4.0 Preamble on Method and Limits

The subject has, to the best of available record, never sustained a formal therapeutic alliance with any clinician. He has been evaluated under carceral conditions at minimum four times (post-Mansion 1986; post-Thunderbolts exposure 1998; post-Liberators 2005; and at least once in the Raft/Pleasant Hill system in the modern era), and on each occasion the recorded notes are conspicuously thin — not because he refused to speak but because he **conducted the interview in the opposite direction**. The evaluators emerge characterized; the subject does not. This is itself a diagnostic datum: a man who walks out of a 90-minute psychiatric intake having learned more about his examiner than the examiner has learned about him is not exhibiting resistance in the clinical sense. He is exhibiting *competence at the task*. He treats clinical interview as adversarial intelligence work and performs accordingly.

The formulation that follows is therefore reconstructed from longitudinal behavioral evidence rather than from self-report. Where self-report exists (the Born Better monologues; the post-exposure Thunderbolts confessions to Songbird and Moonstone; the late-Ellis-era philosophical sequences), it is treated as **performance with informational content** — usable, but not at face value.

A second caveat: the subject's developmental ecology is so unusually pathogenic (disgraced aristocratic title, idealized criminal father, vanished mother, single named family enemy installed in childhood as ontological reference point) that distinguishing *characterological pathology* from *adaptive response to a deranged formation environment* is not entirely possible. The diagnoses below describe the man as he is. They do not pretend he could have become any other man.

---

## 4.1 Primary Diagnosis

### Narcissistic Personality Disorder, Grandiose Subtype, with Obsessional Fixation and Episodic Sadistic Features, on a Dismissive-Avoidant Attachment Substrate

DSM-5 / DSM-5-TR equivalent: **301.81** — meeting at minimum seven of the nine listed criteria, with two criteria (need for admiration; interpersonal exploitativeness) presenting in atypical form requiring elaboration.

ICD-11 equivalent: **6D10.1** (Personality Disorder, severe) with prominent features of **Dissociality** and **Anankastia**, low on **Negative Affectivity**, low on **Detachment** in expressed behavior but high on the *internal* detachment scale, and elevated on the Borderline Pattern qualifier *only* in the narrow domain of Captain-America-adjacent stimuli.

**Criterion-by-criterion behavioral substantiation:**

1. **Grandiose sense of self-importance.** Pervasive and structural rather than episodic. The subject does not boast; he *assumes.* The grandiosity is built into his syntax — he refers to himself in lineage-frame ("a Zemo does not…"), gives commands in the indicative rather than the imperative, and is observably surprised when subordinates require explanation of his decisions. The Citizen V deception required him to *suppress* this presentation for months; the strain shows in the textual record as moments of momentary aristocratic register breaking through (Thunderbolts #4, #7).

2. **Preoccupation with fantasies of unlimited power, brilliance, success.** The world-conquest schemes (Liberators arc; Grandmaster sequence; the Genetic Bomb proposal of the late Thunderbolts run) are not impulses but **rehearsed architectures.** He produces them on cycle, abandons each gracefully when refuted, and produces the next. This is the cognitive signature of a man for whom the fantasy of total order is **continuously running in background** and only periodically pushed to foreground execution.

3. **Belief in being special / understandable only by other high-status individuals.** Demonstrated by his roster selections (Moonstone, the Fixer, the Beetle in his more refined iteration — uniformly high-intellect operatives; the subject does not recruit muscle without an intellect attached), and by his contempt-toned interactions with low-tier criminals, whom he addresses with the patience one extends to children.

4. **Requires excessive admiration.** *Atypical presentation.* The subject does not seek diffuse adulation — crowd-love bores him and the Citizen V period demonstrated he could tolerate it only instrumentally. He seeks the recognition of **a small, qualified audience**: Captain America above all, then a rotating cast of worthy peers. The admiration-need is preserved in full but narrowed in aperture. This is a recognized variant in the Pincus/Lukowitsky pathological narcissism literature (the "covert-overt admixture with selective audience"); it should not be misread as absence of the criterion.

5. **Sense of entitlement.** Pervasive. The title, the resources, the assumption that walking into a room places him at the head of any table within it. The entitlement is genteel rather than tantrumous — he does not demand; he is *baffled* when refused, and the bafflement is genuine, not performed.

6. **Interpersonally exploitative.** Uniform across canon. Every recorded alliance — Masters of Evil, Thunderbolts, V-Battalion overtures, the Bucky operations — is instrumental on his side. Notably, the exploitation is *transparent rather than concealed* in his peer relationships; he expects sophisticated partners to understand they are being used and to use him in return. Concealment is reserved for marks and publics. This is exploitativeness with an aristocrat's manners — which is still exploitativeness.

7. **Lacks empathy.** Affective empathy: absent or near-absent. Cognitive empathy: **elite-tier.** This dissociation is the diagnostically critical configuration. He models other minds at the level of professional psychiatry while remaining functionally indifferent to their experience. The Jarvis sequence is the cleanest demonstration: the subject knew with surgical precision how to maximize Rogers's suffering through Jarvis, which requires accurate modeling of Rogers's interior, and inflicted it with no observable affective resonance.

8. **Often envious of others / believes others envious of him.** Selectively present. He is not envious of wealth, women, or status — he believes himself to possess these by right. He is envious of **Rogers's moral standing** in a way that drives the entire vendetta and that he has never named directly. The reciprocal belief — that others envy him — is calibrated; he assumes intelligent enemies covet his lineage and intellect, and is right often enough to be unfalsifiable.

9. **Arrogant, haughty behaviors and attitudes.** Pervasive but ritualized into courtesy. The arrogance is delivered through formality rather than through coarseness — he does not insult; he **declines to engage**, which lands harder. This is high-functioning aristocratic NPD presentation and is sometimes missed by clinicians trained on the more flamboyant variants.

**Subtype determination.** Grandiose subtype is unambiguous (Cain/Pincus typology). Vulnerable narcissism features (hypersensitivity to slight, shame-driven withdrawal) are minimal in baseline presentation and surface **only** in the narrow window of Cap-proximate stimulus or direct lineage challenge. This pattern — predominant grandiosity with focal vulnerable activation around a single trauma cluster — is the classical Kernbergian "shame-driven grandiosity" profile in which the inflation exists *because* of an underlying wound that must not be touched.

---

## 4.2 Secondary and Co-Morbid Features

### 4.2.1 Obsessional Fixation (sub-syndromal OCPD coloring)

The subject does not meet full Obsessive-Compulsive Personality Disorder criteria — he is not preoccupied with rules at the expense of flexibility, is not miserly, is not rigid about morality (in fact morally fluid in the cynical sense). What he exhibits is **obsessional coloring of the narcissistic structure**, expressed through:

- Single-object fixation across five decades (Rogers).
- Ritualized self-presentation (the hood as ceremonial dress; the sword; the formality of address).
- Eidetic-grade recall deployed almost exclusively in service of the fixation (he remembers Avengers tactical loadouts the way a sommelier remembers vintages).
- Compulsive re-staging of the foundational trauma (Adhesive X mimesis; Mansion-as-paternal-stage; the rooftop fall that re-enacts the father's death).

This is best classified as **obsessional symptom cluster within NPD** rather than co-morbid OCPD. The compulsions are object-bound, not character-bound.

### 4.2.2 Sadistic Features (episodic, target-specific)

Sadistic Personality Disorder was removed from DSM after DSM-III-R and is not a current standalone diagnosis. The features nonetheless require characterization. The subject exhibits sadism that is:

- **Episodic, not pervasive.** Daily-life cruelty is absent. He does not abuse servants, torment subordinates for sport, or seek out suffering as recreation.
- **Target-locked.** Sadism activates almost exclusively in operations directed at Rogers and the Rogers-symbol-set (Jarvis, Barnes, Sarah Rogers's memorabilia).
- **Strategically counterproductive.** This is the key diagnostic feature. He pays operational costs to extract sadistic value — which means the sadism is *not subordinate to the strategic project,* but is a parallel imperative that periodically overrides it. The Mansion operation is the textbook case: the Jarvis spectacle adds nothing to the tactical objective and is the immediate cause of his exposure to the counter-attack window in which Rogers breaks free.

This pattern fits the **"vindicative" subtype** in Millon's sadism typology — sadism organized around grievance rather than around general predatory pleasure. It is comorbid with the NPD rather than constitutive of it.

### 4.2.3 Dismissive-Avoidant Attachment

Not a DSM diagnosis but a foundational structural feature. Evidence reviewed in Section 3; reiterated here as the substrate that makes the NPD self-sustaining. Dismissive-avoidant adults do not present the help-seeking patterns that would otherwise eventually bring narcissistic patients into clinical contact through dysphoric collapse. The subject is therefore **structurally protected from the developmental events that often soften narcissism in midlife** — the loneliness crises, the failed marriages, the children one disappoints. He has none of these.

### 4.2.4 Complex Trauma Substrate (proposed)

The Adhesive X event (Captain America #168) and the longitudinal pre-event load (paternal idealization, paternal death, lineage shame) together constitute a complex trauma profile. Classical PTSD criteria are not fully met because the **re-experiencing is metabolized through agency rather than through intrusion** — he restages the trauma actively rather than suffering it passively. This is a known presentation in high-functioning narcissistic survivors and is sometimes formulated as **"agentic PTSD"** or **"traumatic reenactment without intrusion."** ICD-11 Complex PTSD captures the affect-regulation, self-concept, and interpersonal disturbance domains, though the affect-regulation criterion presents as **rigid over-control** rather than the more typical dysregulation.

Operational consequence: the trauma substrate is the engine of the lifelong campaign. Treatment of the NPD without engagement of the trauma would not, even hypothetically, alter behavior.

---

## 4.3 Differential Diagnosis — What He Is Not, and Why

The following diagnoses have been considered and rejected, each with specific evidentiary grounds. The differential is rigorous because the subject's surface presentation invites lazy attribution and because several of the rejected diagnoses (ASPD in particular) carry operational implications that would mislead a tasking authority.

### 4.3.1 Antisocial Personality Disorder — REJECTED

Surface plausibility: extensive criminal history, indifference to law, manipulation of others, lack of remorse.

Disconfirming evidence:
- **Internal code preserved across decades.** The subject keeps his word in peer dealings to a degree most heroes do not. ASPD does not exhibit principled contract-keeping; it exhibits situational fidelity.
- **Long-horizon planning incompatible with ASPD impulse profile.** The Citizen V deception required months of sustained behavioral inhibition. ASPD patients do not sustain this.
- **Capacity for loyalty to ideas.** The order/hierarchy ideology is consistent across writers and decades; ASPD ideology is typically rhetorical cover rather than organizing principle.
- **No childhood conduct disorder evidence in canon.** Though canon is silent on his pre-debut childhood in detail, the available material describes a heavily structured aristocratic boyhood with tutors, fencing instruction, and intense paternal pedagogy. No truancy, no animal cruelty, no fire-setting, no early-onset rule violation.
- **Criminality is ideological and personal, not characterological.** He commits the crimes he commits *because* of the worldview and the vendetta; he does not commit crimes opportunistically. An ASPD subject in his strategic position would have committed far more incidental crime along the way.

The diagnostic error here is common: ASPD is often misapplied to high-status, high-intellect, criminally productive subjects because their behavior superficially resembles the disorder. The structural psychology is opposite. ASPD is *under-socialized*; this subject is **over-socialized into a deviant aristocratic moral system**.

### 4.3.2 Psychopathy (Hare PCL-R construct) — REJECTED as primary, ACKNOWLEDGED as partial overlap

PCL-R estimated score (reconstructed): **24–28**, well below the 30 cutoff in most jurisdictions. The distribution within facets is the diagnostic finding:

- **Facet 1 (Interpersonal):** elevated — glibness, grandiosity, pathological lying (in operations), manipulativeness.
- **Facet 2 (Affective):** moderately elevated — shallow affect, callousness, failure to accept responsibility; **lower than expected** on lack of remorse (he experiences something at lineage failures that is not remorse but is in the same affective family).
- **Facet 3 (Lifestyle):** low — no impulsivity, no need for stimulation in the psychopathic sense (boredom-vulnerability exists but is differently shaped), no parasitic lifestyle, no irresponsibility, has realistic long-term goals.
- **Facet 4 (Antisocial):** moderately elevated for adult criminality but low for early-onset markers.

The shape — high on interpersonal/affective, low on lifestyle/antisocial — is the **"successful psychopath"** profile in Babiak/Hare terminology, but the lifestyle facet is *so* low that the construct is straining. He is better captured as **NPD with psychopathic features in the interpersonal facet** than as primary psychopathy.

### 4.3.3 Malignant Narcissism (Kernberg construct) — CLOSEST SECONDARY FIT, NOT FULLY MET

Kernberg's malignant narcissism is defined as the syndromal combination of: NPD + antisocial behavior + ego-syntonic aggression/sadism + paranoid orientation.

The subject meets three of four cleanly:
- NPD — yes.
- Antisocial behavior — yes (criminal-operational).
- Ego-syntonic aggression/sadism — yes, in the episodic target-specific form described above.

The fourth — **paranoid orientation** — does not cleanly fit. Kernbergian paranoia in malignant narcissism is *characterological and diffuse*, an organizing suspicion of the world that distorts perception. The subject's distrust is **reality-tested and calibrated**. People genuinely are trying to stop him; subordinates genuinely are likely to defect; institutions genuinely are arrayed against him. His suspicion is operationally proportionate, not distortive.

He therefore sits at the **clinical-narcissistic / malignant-narcissistic border**, with sufficient malignant features to warrant the framework being kept in active consideration but insufficient paranoid distortion to place him in the syndrome proper. Operationally: he is more dangerous than a typical NPD subject and less unhinged than a typical malignant-narcissistic one. He is a malignant narcissist with **intact reality testing**, which makes him harder to provoke into self-defeating paranoia and easier to predict.

### 4.3.4 Schizoid Personality Disorder — REJECTED

Surface plausibility: emotional coolness, limited intimate relationships, indifference to praise/criticism from most sources.

Disconfirming evidence: he performs sociability with virtuosic skill; he actively uses people; he selects romantic partners (rarely, transactionally) rather than avoiding them on aversive grounds; he takes pleasure in aristocratic social ritual (wine, conversation, fencing salons). Schizoid PD is characterized by *aversion to* social engagement; this subject is characterized by *instrumentalization of* social engagement. The avoidance is attachment-style, not schizoid. The interiority is full, not flat.

### 4.3.5 Schizotypal Personality Disorder — REJECTED outright
