No magical thinking, no unusual perceptual experiences, no odd speech, no constricted affect of the schizotypal type, no ideas of reference, no peculiar appearance (the costume is *strategic*, not bizarre in the schizotypal sense). Cognition is exceptionally clear and reality-bound.

### 4.3.6 Delusional Disorder, Grandiose Type — REJECTED

The grandiosity is **empirically overfit, not delusional**. He really is brilliant, well-born (in the legal sense), tactically gifted, and capable of nearly all the things he claims to be capable of. His self-assessments correlate with his actual capabilities to a degree that exceeds the population baseline. The grandiosity exceeds the evidence — the conviction of fitness to rule the planet outpaces any actual rulership demonstration — but the *gap* between claim and capability is the gap of NPD, not of psychotic-spectrum grandiose delusion. He can be argued out of specific tactical overestimations. A delusional patient cannot.

### 4.3.7 Bipolar Spectrum — REJECTED

No episodic mood disturbance. Energy and goal-directed activity are sustained at high levels chronically without depressive trough. The "world-conquest" schemes are sometimes mistaken for grandiose mania; they are stable cognitive products, not phasic. There is no sleep disturbance, no pressured speech, no flight of ideas. He has been observed across years-long stretches of operational quiet (post-Ellis underground period) without depressive collapse — a bipolar profile would have produced one.

### 4.3.8 Major Depressive Disorder — REJECTED for syndrome, ACKNOWLEDGED for trait dysphoria

He does not meet MDD criteria at any documented point. He does exhibit **chronic low-grade dysphoria** around the lineage question and around Cap's continued existence — a kind of background bitterness that occasionally flickers into something resembling melancholy in late-Ellis-era interiority sequences. This is best characterized as **narcissistically defended dysthymia** rather than depressive disorder, and it is a vulnerability that has never been clinically exploited.

### 4.3.9 Post-Traumatic Stress Disorder (classical) — PARTIAL, see 4.2.4

DSM-5 Criterion A trauma exposure: met (the Adhesive X event; cumulative paternal-death context). Re-experiencing: present but transmuted into active reenactment rather than intrusion. Avoidance: present (the mask). Negative alterations in cognition/mood: present but absorbed into the narcissistic structure. Arousal/reactivity: focally present in Cap-proximate situations.

The full classical syndrome is not met; the **complex/agentic variant** is the better characterization. See 4.2.4.

### 4.3.10 Substance Use Disorder — REJECTED

Use is light, ceremonial, instrumental. The mind is the prized organ and he protects it. This is itself a partial diagnostic finding — many high-NPD subjects with his stress load develop substance-mediated affect regulation; his refusal to do so reflects the depth of his cognitive self-investment.

### 4.3.11 Autism Spectrum (high-functioning) — REJECTED

Despite his social distance and ritual rigidity, he reads rooms with elite-tier acuity; he models emotional states in others with precision; he adapts behavior fluidly across social registers (aristocratic salon, criminal underworld, super-team locker room, prison interrogation). The deficit is in *caring* about others' states, not in *perceiving* them. ASD is characterized by perceptual difficulty; he exhibits perceptual mastery with motivational indifference.

### 4.3.12 Dissociative Identity Disorder / Citizen V as Alter — REJECTED

The Citizen V identity is consciously assumed and consciously dropped. It is a cover, not an alter. There is no amnesia between identities, no involuntary switching, no functional separation of memory or skill. It is a *role*, performed with extraordinary fidelity, by a single continuous self.

---

## 4.4 Etiological Reconstruction

The subject's pathology is **expectable rather than mysterious** given the developmental input. The relevant factors, ranked by reconstructed weight:

1. **Idealized criminal father, absent in person, omnipresent in narrative.** Heinrich Zemo is the central object of the household. The subject's developmental task — separation/individuation from the parent — is structurally blocked because the parent is *not available to disappoint him in ordinary ways*. Idealization is never punctured by mundane parental failure. It is punctured only by the catastrophic event of the father's death, which under normal mourning conditions would force reality-testing, but is here weaponized as grievance instead.

2. **Vanished mother (Hilda).** The conspicuous silence about Hilda Zemo across decades of canon is read here as **reflecting the subject's own internal silence**. He has not, on record, named her, mourned her, invoked her, or used her memory in any narrative he constructs. The absence of the maternal counterweight to paternal mythology is the single most pathogenic feature of the developmental ecology — there is no second adult voice in the formative narrative.

3. **Aristocratic title without aristocratic legitimacy.** The Zemos are nominally nobility and substantively pariahs (collaborators, war criminals, post-war exiles). The subject is raised to a station the world refuses to grant him. This **chronic recognition gap** is the precise developmental substrate for grandiose narcissism: a child told he is exceptional by his family and treated as contaminated by the world develops the compensatory belief that the world is wrong.

4. **Named enemy installed in childhood as ontological reference point.** Most children are raised against a constellation of vague proscriptions (don't lie, don't steal). The subject is raised against a *specific living man*. Captain Rogers occupies in his


## Behavioral Atlas

# BEHAVIORAL ATLAS — SUBJECT: HELMUT JULIUS FRITZ ZEMO

## Pre-Synthesis Intelligence File — Section 4 of Dossier

> *Operator's note: this atlas catalogs OBSERVED and INFERRED tells across fifty years of canonical surveillance, organized by ambient condition. Each entry attempts to specify the tell at body-grain — the inch of motion, the half-second of latency, the shift in syntax — that a trained watcher would log. Where canon is explicit, citation is implicit in the main workup; where the atlas extrapolates, it does so from established pattern.*

---

## 1. CALM / AMBIENT BASELINE

Calm is Helmut's natural operational state and the one in which he is least readable, because the persona and the man are aligned. Mark this as the **default profile against which all deviations are measured.**

**Postural baseline.** Vertical spine, shoulders set back without military rigidity — the carriage of a man taught riding and fencing before he was taught to read. Weight distributed evenly across both feet when standing; when seated, he favors the right-hand armrest (sword-side habit, even when unarmed). Knees never crossed in formal company; ankles occasionally. He **does not fidget.** Hands at rest stay at rest — folded, or one resting on the pommel of the family sword, or one wrapped around a glass stem. The absence of fidget is itself a tell: most adults under observation produce micro-movements every nine to fourteen seconds. Helmut can go ninety seconds without one. This is trained, not natural — children fidget. He stopped.

**Vocal baseline.** Mid-to-low register, German-accented English with the consonant edges softened by aristocratic schooling rather than the harder Bavarian working-class profile. Speech pace: deliberately under-tempo, approximately 110–125 words per minute against an adult average near 160. He **lets sentences land.** Punctuation is audible. He does not fill silences; the silences are part of the sentence.

**Gaze pattern.** Long fixations (3–6 seconds typical) followed by deliberate breaks — he looks away to grant the other party room to speak, then returns. He does not do the dominance-stare common to lesser tacticians. He does, however, scan the room on entry in a clockwise sweep that finishes on the highest-status occupant. Total entry scan: under two seconds. He will later be able to reproduce the room's contents — exits, occupant count, ordnance — from memory.

**Microhabits in calm.**
- A slow, single exhale through the nose when transitioning between topics. Not a sigh. A reset.
- Right thumb periodically traces the signet of the family ring on his right ring finger — once, twice, then stops. This is the most consistent tell across all conditions and the closest he gets to self-soothing. Frequency rises under cognitive load; remains light in calm.
- When listening, the head tips approximately 8–12 degrees to the left, then returns. Not "active listening" theater; it is the angle at which he prefers to record.
- A drink — wine, brandy, water — is sipped, never gulped. Glass returned to the same coordinate within a centimeter each time. Watch for the *coaster-precision*.
- He reads in straight lines and turns pages with the index finger of whichever hand is not holding the volume; the other hand stays still on his thigh.

**Conversational behavior.** Asks more questions than he answers. Compliments are specific, brief, and accurate ("Your placement of the second flank was correct; the third was not"). Insult, in calm, is **never present** — the insulting Helmut is the destabilized Helmut. Calm Helmut praises and observes.

**Decisional habit in calm.** He defers decisions he is not forced to make. Time is his ally; he prefers to let a situation declare more of itself before committing. When he commits, he commits without revisiting — the deliberation is front-loaded, the execution silent.

---

## 2. PLANNING / STRATEGIC ABSORPTION

A distinct sub-mode of calm, observable when he is constructing or revising an operation.

**Posture shifts.** He stands more than he sits. If pacing, the path is a closed rectangle, not a line — corners taken at right angles, stride length consistent to within two centimeters per pass. He paces clockwise. (Counter-clockwise pacing is a stress tell — see §4.)

**Verbal-internal behavior.** He talks to himself in **German** when alone, **French** when irritated by his own slowness, **English** when rehearsing speech for an English-speaking target. Language selection is the cleanest available index of his internal posture for any observer who has placed a microphone.

**Material habits.** Prefers physical maps and three-dimensional models over screens for top-level planning; uses screens for logistics and intelligence intake. He sketches. The sketches are accurate, small, technical — fortification cross-sections, vector arrows, kill-funnels — and he annotates them in three or four languages on the same page depending on which language carries the relevant technical vocabulary most cleanly. He destroys them after use; he does not archive his own thinking on paper.

**Eating pattern in planning mode.** Light, cold, ritual — bread, a hard cheese, fruit. He does not stop to eat; he eats while continuing to work, with the same coaster-precision applied to crumbs (a folded napkin, never the desk). The body is fueled, not indulged.

**Sleep pattern in planning mode.** Compresses to four-to-five hours, split into two cycles where possible — a mid-evening sleep of ninety minutes and a pre-dawn sleep of three hours. He emerges from both fully oriented; no grogginess on record. The split-cycle pattern is medieval-aristocratic and he is aware of the historical lineage; it pleases him.

---

## 3. SOCIAL / FORMAL ENGAGEMENT

Operating in rooms with peers, dignitaries, or marks.

**Entrance behavior.** Arrives within a window of three to seven minutes after the nominal start — late enough to be noticed, early enough not to insult. Does not announce himself; allows the room to recognize him. Greets the host first, then the highest-status guest, then sweeps outward by descending status with metronome regularity. He **never skips a tier** — to do so would signal disorder.

**Handshake.** Firm, brief, single pump. Withdraws the hand at the apex, never lets the other party complete the cycle. The handshake is a punctuation mark, not a transaction. With women he is canonically older-European: a slight bow at the neck, no actual hand-kiss in modern company unless the woman is herself titled.

**Use of titles.** He uses other people's titles correctly and unprompted, including obscure ones. This is currency he spends generously because it costs him nothing and it tells targets they are recognized. His own title he allows others to use without correction and never insists upon — the man who insists on his title has not yet earned it.

**Compliments and barbs.** In formal social settings, every compliment is specific and verifiable; every barb is delivered as a compliment with one word turned. Watch the **adjective slot** in his sentences; the lever almost always sits there. "An *imaginative* response to a question that was, perhaps, not asked" — the operative word is "imaginative," and the listener will replay it for hours.

**Drinking pattern.** One full glass over the duration of the function. He sips on the same intervals he uses in calm baseline, regardless of conversational intensity. The glass is a metronome. He does not drink to keep up; he drinks to mark time.

**Departure behavior.** Leaves on a quiet upbeat — never on a low note, never at peak attention. He prefers to be the second-most-recent topic of conversation rather than the most. He says goodbye to fewer people than he said hello to, and only to those whose future utility he has decided upon.

---

## 4. STRESS — LOW TO MODERATE (operational complexity, no symbolic content)

This is the band in which he performs **best.** Tactical reverses, intelligence failures, betrayals by subordinates whose loyalty he had not over-invested — these are all metabolized cleanly.

**Postural tells.** Stillness *increases.* Where calm Helmut produces a micro-movement every ninety seconds, stressed-operational Helmut produces one every two to three minutes. The signet-trace habit slows; the inhale-pause-exhale lengthens. He is downshifting voluntarily.

**Verbal tells.** Sentences shorten. The accent rounds slightly — under cognitive load the German vowel system reasserts itself in the English word, and "v" begins to colonize "w" again ("vill" for "will" creeps in around the third hour of a long operation). He becomes **more polite,** not less — please and thank-you density rises, particularly with subordinates. This is not warmth; it is conservation of crew morale, calculated as one calculates fuel.

**Decision velocity.** Increases. He makes faster, cleaner calls in this band than in calm — calm is for inhabiting options, stress is for choosing among them. He delegates more aggressively under operational stress, because the cost of micromanagement now exceeds the cost of subordinate error.

**Eating and sleeping under operational stress.** Both compress further. Sleep drops to three hours. He maintains hydration with discipline — water glass within reach at all times — because dehydrated cognition is the first failure mode he has identified in himself and he respects the data.

---

## 5. STRESS — HIGH, IMPERSONAL (existential threat to plan, not self)

The band where a complex scheme is collapsing for structural reasons — a Songbird turning, a Moonstone defecting, an Avengers mobilization arriving early.

**The pacing reverses to counter-clockwise.** This is the single most reliable index that internal state has crossed from operational to anxious. A trained observer should log it within two passes.

**Glove behavior.** He adjusts the cuffs of his gloves — first the left, then the right, then the left again — at intervals of roughly forty seconds. This is a self-grooming displacement and it is the closest he comes in this band to a public tell. He is unaware of it; or he is aware of it and tolerates it because suppressing it would cost focus.

**Language drift.** German irrupts mid-sentence in English speech — usually a noun, occasionally an interjection. "Das ist —" cut off, restarted in English. He hears himself do it and does not punish himself for it; he registers it as data about his own state.

**Vocal shift.** Pitch *drops* further. Most people's pitch rises under stress; his descends. He has trained against the rising-pitch response and overshoots. The resulting register is the calmest he ever sounds, and it is **the danger signal** to anyone who has watched him long enough.

**Decision habit.** He becomes more willing to abandon assets. The man who would not waste a pawn in calm will sacrifice a knight in this band without flinching. This is correct play and he knows it, but the threshold for "asset" lowers — subordinates who were valued in calm become expendable in this band, which is one of the reasons his retinues have a high turnover.

---

## 6. STRESS — HIGH, SYMBOLIC (Rogers, Barnes, the Zemo name, the mask)

The catastrophic band. The entire pre-synthesis workup identifies this as the failure mode that has cost him every major confrontation.

**The strategic IQ drops, observably, in roughly the following sequence:**

1. **First 30 seconds:** posture becomes *more* erect, not less. He squares to the threat. The right hand drifts to the sword pommel and stays there. Vocal pitch drops further still — sub-baseline. He believes he is in control.
2. **30 seconds to 5 minutes:** the speech becomes *more elaborate,* not less. Sentences lengthen. Subordinate clauses proliferate. He begins to deliver the speech he has rehearsed since adolescence. This is the **monologue tell** and it is functionally identical to a tactical pause for the opponent.
3. **5 to 20 minutes:** he selects the symbolic action over the strategic action. The hostage is beaten in front of the witness; the family weapon is chosen over the efficient weapon; the mimetic act is preferred over the lethal one. **The signature error is to convert the operation into a tableau.**
4. **20 minutes onward:** the tableau is disrupted, usually by exactly the variable the symbolic frame had asked him to ignore (Cap's physical capacity, a subordinate's conscience, a bystander's intervention). At this point his behavior becomes brittle-erratic — the controlled register breaks into something close to a snarl, and a high-altitude fall, a vat, or a rooftop is somewhere in the next two pages.

**The cluster of physical tells in this band:**
- The signet-ring trace becomes a *grip,* not a trace — he closes the right thumb and forefinger around the ring and holds.
- A muscle at the left jaw — the masseter — visibly engages and releases on a slow rhythm. Through a hood this is invisible; through a removed hood, it is the most readable thing on the face.
- The left eye narrows fractionally more than the right when he is focusing rage. Asymmetric squint, left-dominant.
- Breathing audibly deepens through the nose. He does not pant. He *aerates,* on a four-count.

**He does not shout.** He has never been documented shouting in symbolic-stress mode. The voice goes the other way — to a near-whisper, intended to make the room lean in. The whisper is the danger.

---

## 7. THREAT — DIRECT PHYSICAL

The fencing-trained Helmut. Distinct from §6, though §6 can resolve into §7 if the symbolic confrontation collapses into a fight.

**Footwork.** Classical fencing stance unconsciously assumed before any anticipated melee — lead foot pointed at the threat, rear foot perpendicular, knees softened. Weight on the balls of the feet, not the heels. He **does not square up** in a boxer's stance; he is an edged-weapon fighter and presents the narrow profile.

**Hand carriage.** Sword hand floats free, never gripping in advance — the draw is faster from rest than from grip, and he knows it. Off-hand is held slightly forward, palm down, used for parries and distance-measurement.

**Verbal behavior in combat.** He talks. Not taunts in the genre sense; *measured remarks,* often complimentary. "Good." "Better than the last time." "You have improved your second intention." He is annotating the bout aloud, partly to unsettle the opponent who hears himself being graded mid-fight, partly because the sub-vocalization helps him track tempo.

**Pain response.** Minimal external. Takes cuts without flinching above the eyebrow level — the eyebrows do not move. He registers wounds with a downward glance and a recalculation, not a sound. This is trained and it is also a tell: a normal person flinches, and the absence of flinch is, paradoxically, identifying.

**Decision habit under direct physical threat.** Disengage if the encounter is asymmetric in his favor (waste no exposure); engage if it is roughly even (he trusts his blade); **disengage with theatrical cost** if it is asymmetric against him (he will throw a flash, a smoke, a hostage to buy the exit). He does not die for points.

---

## 8. THREAT — INDIRECT / SURVEILLANCE PRESSURE

When he believes he is being watched, hunted, or analyzed.

**Behavior is paradoxically more relaxed at the surface.** He performs ease for the watcher. The signet-trace returns to calm-baseline cadence; the drink-metronome resumes. The persona thickens.

**However:** route variation. He stops repeating walking paths. Restaurants chosen for sight-lines to entrances. The clockwise-entry-scan becomes more elaborate — two passes instead of one. He selects seats with backs to walls and exits behind him at oblique angles. None of this is unusual for trained personnel; what is **diagnostic** is that he does it *gracefully,* without the stiffness most surveilled subjects telegraph.

**Verbal cleanup.** He becomes terser with subordinates over any monitored channel; complex operational discussion moves to in-person or to one-time-pad equivalents. He assumes interception and writes for the intercepting reader, occasionally seeding deliberate false signal for the pleasure of misdirection.

---

## 9. INTIMACY (rare; transactional; instructive)

Canon offers few examples, which is itself the most important datum. Where intimacy is observable:

**Sexual / romantic behavior.** Brief liaisons, almost always with women of approximate or superior status, almost always in service of an operational frame (information, alliance, leverage on a third party). He is competent at the performance — courtly, attentive, generous in small ways — and disengages cleanly. **No post-encounter behavior** is documented (no second meetings absent operational reason, no correspondence, no return). He treats sex as a category of dinner.

**Non-sexual intimacy (peer respect).** With Moonstone and, occasionally, Osborn — figures he regards as cognitively serious — he relaxes the formality fractionally. He will sit, where with subordinates he stands. He will let a sentence trail, where with subordinates every sentence is finished. He uses given names. He occasionally **agrees in silence** rather than verbally — a slight nod across a room — which is the highest social courtesy he offers a living person.

**Affection toward objects.** The sword, the ring, certain volumes in his library — these receive a register of care that no human in his life has been documented receiving. He handles them slowly. He polishes the sword himself; he does not delegate that.

**The intimacy tell, when it occurs.** A drop in vocal pace below even his slow baseline — under 100 words per minute. The man with whom he is speaking has been **identified as someone he will not lie to in this moment.** It is exceptionally rare and worth logging when observed.

---

## 10. GRIEF

Canon almost never permits him to grieve openly. The atlas must therefore read the behavior around losses for their grief content.

**Heinrich's death (pre-debut).** The entire subsequent career is the grief, intellectualized. There is no narrower behavioral window.

**Failure of the Thunderbolts (Songbird's choice, the team's defection).** Documented response: a withdrawal, a period of solitary planning, the appearance of a colder and more philosophical Helmut on the other side. **No tears, no rage scene.** The grief is metabolized into ideology.

**Inferred tells under grief.** Increased solitude. The pacing rectangle becomes a slow loop. The pacing becomes counter-clockwise — the same tell as high-impersonal stress, because grief is filed under that category in his system. The wine ration increases from one glass per evening to two, never three. The signet-trace becomes a slow circle rather than the usual back-and-forth. He reads more, sleeps less, eats indifferently. Subordinates report him as "courteous as ever, but absent" — the surface persona maintains while the interior recomputes.

**He does not visit graves.** He does not mark anniversaries observably. He is not, on the evidence, a man who returns to wounds in any commemorative sense; he returns to them by **continuing to act on them.** Action is his mourning.

---

## 11. VICTORY

**Behavior at the moment of operational success.** Quiet. He does not crow. The most documented response to a clean strategic win is a single exhale through the nose — the same reset-exhale from calm baseline — and a redirection of attention to the *next* problem. Victory is metabolized as completion of a task, not as triumph.

**Behavior at the moment of personal vengeance success.** Different. The whisper deepens. He **lingers.** This is the diagnostic difference between the strategist and the avenger: the strategist exits the room; the avenger stays to watch. When Helmut stays in the room after a win, he is in vendetta mode, and he is also, *in that lingering,* squandering the win — because every documented catastrophic reversal in his career has occurred in the minutes after he stayed too long.

**Tells of internal pleasure.** Almost none facial — he is hooded most of the time and trained besides. The pleasure surfaces as **verbal elaboration:** the post-victory monologue, the explanation to the defeated, the recital of the chain of reasoning that led to this moment. The monologue is the pleasure. It is also, repeatedly, the loss vector — because the monologue is the time the opponent uses to escape, recover, or hit back.

**No documented celebration of any kind.** No raised arms, no toast, no embrace. He has won large and small for fifty years and the body does not yet have a vocabulary for joy.

---

## 12. DEFEAT

**Acute defeat (the fight is lost).** He withdraws cleanly when he can; he accepts custody with composure when he cannot. He does **not** beg. He does not bargain at the surface — he bargains structurally, through patience, through the long game of reputation and legal process and the eventual prison break.

**The defeat-posture.** Spine remains erect. The chin does not drop. He looks his captors in the face. He uses their titles. This is not bravado; it is the assertion that even in defeat he ranks above them by birth and intellect, and the assertion is the consolation.

**Verbal defeat behavior.** He is *more* articulate after losing than after winning. He explains. He explains to himself, to the captor, to the interrogator, occasionally to Rogers. The explanation has the structure of an after-action report; it does not have the structure of an apology, because the concept does not arrive cleanly to him.

**Behavior in custody.** Exemplary, in a way that unsettles staff. He keeps his cell clean. He requests books and is specific about editions. He learns the guards' names and uses them correctly. He out-talks his evaluators by a margin that is itself diagnostic — he studies the clinician as the clinician thinks the clinician is studying him, and he is faster. He never breaks the persona of the courteous prisoner, and the persona's seamlessness is what eventually frightens the long-term observers.

**The defeat tell that matters most.** *He plans the next operation in custody.* No fallow period. The mind is already on the next architecture before the cell door closes. Any prison psychiatrist who logs him as "improving" or "resigned" has been outflanked.

---

## 13. BOREDOM

Underweighted in the assessment literature, foregrounded here.

**Tells.** The signet-trace accelerates and becomes irregular — the consistent rhythm of stressed-Helmut breaks into a syncopated tap. He reads more, then re-reads, then puts books down at unaccustomed angles. He **rearranges objects on his desk** — a habit that does not appear in any other state. He drinks earlier in the day. The eating ritual slackens; crumbs are tolerated.

**Decisional consequence.** A Helmut Zemo with nothing strategically interesting to do invents something cruel. The boredom-to-cruelty pipeline is short — under a week in confined settings, under a month at liberty. He will provoke a subordinate, escalate a minor grievance, reopen a closed account. The cruelty is **not pleasurable in itself** in this mode; it is *generative* — it produces complication, and complication produces something for the mind to chew.

**The defense against his own boredom is the largest single risk factor in his behavioral profile.** Any handler, captor, or analyst seeking to predict his next move should weight the *interestingness gradient* of his environment as heavily as any strategic variable.

---

## 14. ENCOUNTER WITH ROGERS — SPECIFIC PROTOCOLS

The Cap-presence overrides all other state. Catalogued separately because the override is total.

- **Within


## Daily Life, Routines & Rituals

# DOSSIER SECTION — DAILY LIFE, ROUTINES & RITUALS

## SUBJECT: HELMUT JULIUS FRITZ ZEMO (BARON ZEMO II)

*What a week of continuous surveillance would record. Reconstructed from canonical behavior, residential patterns established across Stern, Busiek, Nicieza, Gage, Ellis, Brubaker, and the Spencer/Zub runs; supplemented by inferences consistent with the operator-canon presentation (full purple cowl, green military tunic, sabre at hip, aristocratic European register).*

---

## 1. THE ARCHITECTURE OF A DAY — BASELINE (NON-OPERATIONAL PERIODS)

When Subject is not in an active campaign cycle — i.e., between schemes, between prison terms, in a "wintering" phase at one of the surviving Zemo properties or a leased shadow-residence — his day is the day of a 19th-century European officer transposed into the 21st century. It is **monastic, scheduled to the quarter-hour, and almost entirely silent.** Surveillance teams who have run him for more than a week consistently report that the most striking quality of the man is **how little ambient noise he generates.** No music in the residence. No television. No radio. No phone conversation conducted on speaker. Doors close with a hand on them, not by their own weight. He is audible only when he chooses to be.

**04:50–05:10 — Wake.** No alarm. The subject wakes within a twenty-minute window without external prompting and has done so since adolescence (military-academy conditioning, retained). He does not linger in bed; the transition from sleep to vertical is under thirty seconds. Bedding is squared before he leaves the room — not made decoratively, but folded as a cadet folds a footlocker. Single pillow. No bed-partner ever observed across multi-week surveillance windows.

**05:10–05:40 — Ablutions and dress.** Subject does not look at his unmasked face in the mirror during washing. He shaves by feel, with a straight razor, having mapped the topography of the scarring so thoroughly that he does not require sight. The mirror in the primary bath is angled so that a man of his height sees the wall behind him and not his own reflection — this is a deliberate installation, not an accident. He dresses fully before leaving the bedroom suite, even when alone in a sealed residence. **He is never observed in a state of undress in any room not designated for it.** The cowl is not worn for morning routines inside a secured residence; in private he goes bare-faced but rarely passes a reflective surface without averting.

**05:40–06:30 — Reading, in silence, in a fixed chair.** Always the same chair in a given residence — high-backed, leather, positioned to face the room's entrance (he does not sit with his back to a door, ever, and surveillance teams use this as a verification cue when identifying him from posture alone in low-resolution feeds). Reading material is rotated on a weekly cycle: Mondays and Thursdays, military history (Clausewitz, Jomini, Liddell Hart, Beaufre — annotated copies, marginalia in three languages); Tuesdays and Fridays, philosophy (Schmitt, Nietzsche, Spengler, and — diagnostically — Marcus Aurelius, the only moralist he reads without contempt); Wednesdays, poetry (Rilke, Hölderlin, George — German Romantic and proto-fascist registers, in the original); Saturdays, primary historical sources concerning the Zemo line specifically; Sundays, contemporary intelligence and political journalism in four languages, read clinically, the way a butcher reads a carcass.

He does not underline. He marks with a small pencilled vertical bar in the outer margin. A double bar indicates he disagrees and intends to return.

**06:30–08:00 — Physical conditioning.** This is the longest single block of his day and the most invariant. The régime is broken into three sub-phases:

- **06:30–07:00 — Calisthenic and flexibility base.** Bodyweight work performed in a long sequence without rest: pull-ups, dips, single-leg squats, planks, hanging leg raises. Old-school. No music. He counts in German, under his breath, and a long-range microphone will pick up the count if the room is otherwise sealed.
- **07:00–07:40 — Fencing practice.** Sabre primarily; épée twice weekly. Solo drills against a mounted target or, when available, a live partner of qualified rank (during Thunderbolts residence periods, this was occasionally Atlas, more often a hired master). The drills are *forms* — historical Hungarian sabre, German academic Mensur footwork, classical Italian. He does not invent. He inherits. The blade he uses for practice is not the family sabre but a working duplicate; the family blade is drawn only operationally or ceremonially.
- **07:40–08:00 — Cool-down and breath work.** Slow, controlled. He has a near-resting heart rate within ninety seconds of his last exertion. This is observable and a useful biometric tell.

**08:00–08:30 — First meal.** Light. Black coffee (Viennese-style, prepared by his own hand even when staff are present — he does not trust others to set the temperature of what enters his body), one boiled egg, dark bread, occasionally a small portion of cured ham or smoked fish. The meal is eaten at a table, with utensils, from porcelain, regardless of whether anyone is watching. **He never eats standing. He never eats walking. He never eats with his hands.** Surveillance teams have used the willingness to grab food with fingers as a reliable negative-identification test for impersonators.

**08:30–12:00 — The "work" block.** This is the operational core of any given day and the most variable in content, but the most rigid in structure. He sits, he reads, he writes, he calls. Whatever the active project — a cell to be cultivated, an asset to be turned, a Zemo-archive document to be authenticated, a Cap movement to be tracked — it is conducted in this block. He uses an old leather-bound notebook for first-pass thinking (later destroyed; the page count of his discarded notebooks per month is a usable activity proxy) and a typed clean copy for any document that will survive the day. **Handwriting is small, upright, German cursive, ink-fountain.** He does not use ballpoints if a fountain pen is available.

Phone use is brief, formal, and conducted in whichever language the counterparty's tradecraft demands. Calls rarely exceed four minutes. He hangs up first. He does not say goodbye.

**12:00–12:30 — Walk.** Always a walk. Outdoors when the residence permits, on a fixed indoor circuit when it does not. The walk is a thinking exercise, not exercise — he covers the same route at the same pace and uses the locomotion as a metronome for analysis. A surveillance team that maps the circuit can predict to within five seconds where he will be at any moment of the walk. He carries a walking stick (sword-cane when operational, plain when not) and gloves regardless of weather.

**12:30–13:15 — Midday meal.** The principal meal of the day in the European fashion. Cooked from raw ingredients, almost always by his own hand when in residence — he is a competent, traditional cook (game, root vegetables, dark sauces; almost no Italian or Asian repertoire, almost no improvisation). Wine, one glass, occasionally two; **never to the point of measurable cognitive softening,** which surveillance audio confirms by the stability of his sentence-construction across the post-meal hour. Table linen. Cloth napkin folded after.

**13:15–14:00 — Correspondence and dead-letter work.** Physical mail, hand-written. He maintains a small number of standing correspondents — fellow aristocrats of various states of disgrace, two academics in unrelated fields (a medievalist and a fencing-master historian), at least one priest whose name surveillance has never confirmed. Letters are dropped at varied posting locations on a rotation he has used for decades; the rotation is not random but rule-based, and the rule has not been reverse-engineered by any agency that has tried.

**14:00–17:00 — Variable. Operational or scholarly.** In an active campaign, this is meeting/movement time. In a wintering phase, this is **archive work** — the Zemo lineage research that culminated in the *Born Better* findings is not a discrete project; it is ongoing, lifelong, and he adds to it weekly. He has cross-referenced his ancestors' deeds against six centuries of European criminal and judicial record. The archive lives in three physical locations and one cryptographic backup; he has never digitized it primarily, because he does not trust the medium and because **the act of writing it by hand is part of the ritual.**

**17:00–18:00 — Second physical block, lighter.** Long stretching, breath work, sometimes a second short fencing session, occasionally pistol or rifle dry-fire (he is a competent but not exceptional shooter — the sword is the loved instrument; firearms are tools).

**18:00–19:30 — Evening meal and the only social window of the day.** When alone, eaten quietly, with reading. When with subordinates or guests, conducted at table with formal service. He hosts well, in the European tradition — a Helmut Zemo dinner is structured (aperitif, three courses, digestif), the conversation is steered by him without his appearing to steer, and guests almost universally report afterward that they enjoyed themselves and revealed more than they intended. This is not magic. It is the deliberate use of courtesy as an interrogation technique. He has used it on Moonstone, on Songbird, on Osborn, and — in *Thunderbolts* canon — on at least three captive subjects who were nominally his prisoners and did not realize they were being debriefed.

**19:30–22:00 — Cultural / restorative block.** Reading (the day's second reading is always different from the morning's — if the morning was strategic, the evening is aesthetic). Music, occasionally, but only live or on physical media, never streamed — primarily Wagner, Mahler, Bruckner, some Bach, almost no opera by post-Wagnerian composers, almost no music written after 1945. He listens with the lights low and the cowl off. This is the closest the file comes to recording **leisure proper** — a state in which he is not pursuing anything.

**22:00–22:30 — Final patrol and security check.** Personally walks the residence. Tests doors, checks sightlines, examines two or three security positions he has memorized as canaries. He does not trust electronic security alone; **he wants the building to feel the same to his body at night as it did in the morning, and any drift is information.**

**22:30 — Bed.** No reading in bed. No device in the room. Lights out within five minutes of lying down. He sleeps approximately six and a half hours and has done so for decades. No recorded sleep complaint. He wakes once or twice per night, briefly, then resumes sleep — surveillance via thermal/biometrics confirms this pattern as stable across years.

---

## 2. HABITS OF PLACE

He has a **strong territorial relationship to specific rooms.** In any residence he occupies for more than a fortnight, the following emerge:

- **A "command" room** — the room in which the day's strategic block occurs. Always near a window, never the master bedroom, always with line of sight to the principal entrance. Within a week of arrival, the chairs in this room have been physically rearranged.
- **A "blade" room** — where the family sabre rests when not on his person. This is treated with reverence. He enters it bare-headed. The sabre is laid (not hung) on a cloth-covered surface; he inspects and oils it on a weekly schedule (Sunday evenings, without fail).
- **An "archive" corner** — three or four shelves of working documents and the current notebook. He is the only person ever observed handling these volumes.
- **An "unoccupied" room** — every residence has one room he does not use. Surveillance teams have noted this anomaly repeatedly. It is hypothesized (not confirmed) that the unused room corresponds to a function — a child's room, a wife's parlor, a mother's morning-room — that he is not permitting himself.

**He paces a left-handed circuit** when thinking — counter-clockwise around a table or a room. The handedness of the circuit is consistent across continents and decades. A surveillance team in 1997 (Thunderbolts-era safehouse) and a surveillance team in the modern Sokovian arc both recorded the same counter-clockwise pattern, same shoulder-drop, same brief touch of the right hand to the hilt of the sword on each pass of a particular axis. **He is not aware he does this.** It is one of the few unconscious tells in his repertoire.

---

## 3. HABITS OF TIME

**He is punctual to the minute** for any appointment he has set. He is **deliberately late** — by a calculated and consistent five to seven minutes — to any appointment set by another party of equal or lower rank, as a status assertion. Subordinates have learned this and budget for it. With superiors-by-station (a head of state, the genuine V-Battalion leadership when he was pretending to court them), he is two minutes early.

**He observes the date.** Not birthdays — neither his own nor others' — but historical anniversaries. Surveillance teams have noted that on specific dates he is unusually quiet, drinks a single additional glass of wine at the evening meal, and occasionally removes a particular volume from a particular shelf. Cross-referencing these dates yields:

- The date of Heinrich Zemo's death in the South American jungle (Avengers #15 in-universe equivalent).
- The date of his own Adhesive X immersion.
- The fall of Berlin, 1945.
- A date in late autumn that has never been correlated to any public event and is presumed personal — possibly the mother's death, possibly something earlier.

He does not mark Christmas. He marks no religious observance despite the priest correspondent. He does not mark his own birthday in any observed manner; subordinates who have wished him one have been received with a politeness so cold it has been described in post-debrief by a former Thunderbolt as "being thanked by a wall."

---

## 4. THE MASK — DAILY DISCIPLINE

The cowl is **donned the moment he leaves any residence and is not removed in any non-secured space, ever.** The process of putting it on is itself ritualized: he holds it for a moment in both hands before drawing it over his head — a beat that surveillance video has captured dozens of times and that has the quality of a religious vestment being assumed rather than a costume being worn. The ragged lower edge is adjusted twice (once at the front seam, once at the nape). The high collar of the tunic is then drawn up to meet it. **The transition from Helmut to Zemo takes approximately fourteen seconds and is performed standing, facing away from any mirror.**

He owns multiples — at least four cowls in rotation, treated as a uniformed officer treats his service caps. They are hand-cleaned. He does not delegate this. The seam down the front is inspected weekly for wear; a frayed seam is grounds for retiring the garment. The retired cowls are not discarded; they are kept, folded, in a single drawer whose contents only he handles.

When the cowl is off — in residence, in secured space — he often unconsciously reaches up and touches his temple or the bridge of his nose, as if to verify the absence. This is one of the few **somatic tics** that breaches his composure, and it appears more frequently when he is fatigued or after long stretches of operational masking.

---

## 5. WORK PATTERNS — OPERATIONAL TEMPO

When a campaign is active, the day reshapes around it but the **structural scaffolding does not break.** The 04:50 wake, the conditioning block, the meals at their hours, the evening security walk — these are non-negotiable. He has been observed conducting strategic planning at 09:00 on the day of a major operation with the demeanor of a man balancing his accounts. **Battle is, for him, a scheduled appointment.**

Within operations he exhibits a distinct **escalation cadence** observable across decades: a long planning phase (weeks to years) in which he is exceptionally productive and behaviorally stable; an execution phase in which he is calm and effective; and — if the operation touches Cap personally — a terminal "flourish" phase in which his schedule visibly fractures. He skips the morning reading. He paces more. He eats less. He delivers a speech that did not need to be delivered. The Jarvis episode is the textbook case; the Adhesive X vat is the original. **A surveillance team that observes the morning reading being skipped two days in a row should escalate to immediate alert: he is approaching the flourish.**

---

## 6. DOWNTIME — WHAT HE DOES WHEN HE DOES NOT HAVE TO DO ANYTHING

This is the hardest section to populate because **he is rarely in a true downtime state.** When forced into one — imprisonment, exile, deliberate wintering — the observed behaviors are:

- **Translation work.** He has, across multiple incarceration arcs, occupied himself by translating texts (Tacitus into German, Goethe into Russian, his own Zemo-archive notes into French as a memorization exercise). He treats translation the way other men treat crossword puzzles.
- **Chess, against himself, by correspondence with one of the academic correspondents, and — rarely — over the board with a guest. He plays a classical, positional game; openings of choice are the Queen's Gambit Declined as White, the Caro-Kann as Black. He does not blunder. He does not enjoy fast games.
- **Fencing forms** at a meditative tempo. The same drills, slower.
- **Walking.** Longer than the noon circuit. He has been observed walking for two and three hours through forest or city without apparent purpose, returning composed.
- **Sitting.** Genuinely sitting, doing nothing, for thirty to sixty minutes at a stretch. Eyes open. He is not meditating in any technical sense — he is *thinking,* but with the brake on, letting material surface.

He does not engage with screens recreationally. He does not have hobbies in the consumer sense. He does not collect (beyond books and one specific category of historical document). He does not garden, despite owning land. He does not own a pet — the closest the file comes is a period during the Ellis-era retreat when he was observed feeding crows from a windowsill on a daily schedule for several weeks. The crows came on time. He did not name them.

---

## 7. SOCIAL CONTACT — THE TEXTURE OF A WEEK

A representative week of pure surveillance, in a non-operational phase, would log the following human contacts:

- **Daily:** a housekeeper or steward, treated with formal courtesy and addressed by surname. Exchanges are functional, brief, and warm only at the edges. He pays well. He notices a change in their gait or expression and inquires, once, and remembers the answer.
- **Two to three times per week:** the local merchant from whom he buys bread, the dealer from whom he buys wine, the cutler who maintains his blades. He goes to them; they do not come to him. He pays in cash. He speaks the local language at native fluency or near it.
- **Once per week:** a fencing partner if one is locally available.
- **Once per week, on average:** a phone call to a correspondent at distance. Under five minutes. He hangs up first.
- **Once per fortnight, on average:** a longer meeting — a former subordinate seeking audience, a broker of information, a courier. Conducted at table, with formal service.
- **Zero times per week:** a friend. The file contains no figure to whom this word can be honestly applied.

The week contains **no spontaneity in the human sense.** He has not been observed accepting an unplanned social invitation in canonical record. He does not encounter people; he meets them.

---

## 8. AMBIENT MICRO-PATTERNS — THE FILE'S FINE GRAIN

Compiled from cross-referenced surveillance traces (audio, video, satellite, HUMINT debrief):

- **Posture in repose:** seated upright, hands resting on the thighs or one hand on the pommel of a stick or sword, feet flat, weight even. The "officer at rest" posture. He does not slouch. He does not cross his legs in the American manner; if he crosses them, it is at the ankle.
- **Stride:** measured, slightly heel-led, length consistent regardless of urgency. He does not visibly hurry. In actual emergencies he moves quickly but his gait does not lose its quality; the cadence increases without the geometry changing.
- **Hands:** dominant in his self-presentation. Gloved in public almost without exception. Bare hands at table only. He uses his hands to punctuate but never to gesticulate broadly; the gestures are small, precise, often at the level of the chest.
- **Voice:** mid-range, controlled, slightly resonant under the cowl. He speaks more slowly than the median speaker of any language he uses. He does not raise his voice in argument; volume drops as stakes rise. **A whispering Zemo is a maximally dangerous Zemo.**
- **Eye contact:** sustained, level, neither aggressive nor warm. He does not break gaze first in social situations. In operational interrogation he uses gaze as a pressure instrument.
- **Laughter:** rare. Real laughter, almost never. When he laughs strategically — at a guest's pleasantry, to lubricate a meeting — it is brief, vocal, unsmiling around the eyes. Surveillance audio archived approximately three instances across an aggregated operational year of recording.
- **Touch:** minimal. He does not initiate physical contact except handshakes (firm, brief, gloved) and, ceremonially, the kiss of greeting in certain European registers. He has not been observed embracing another human being in any recorded canon.
- **Tells under stress:** the right hand drifts to the sword-hilt or, when no sword is worn, to the right hip where the sword would be. The free hand may touch the temple beneath the cowl. The voice softens. The morning reading is skipped. The counter-clockwise pacing accelerates without changing direction.

---

## 9. WHAT A WEEK OF SURVEILLANCE WOULD MISS

A team running him for seven days and writing a report on the eighth would conclude, accurately, that he is **predictable, regimented, austere, cultured, dangerous, and lonely without acknowledging loneliness.** They would have his routes, his hours, his suppliers, his correspondents, his blade-maintenance schedule, the angle of his bath mirror.

They would miss the following, because these emerge only on a horizon of months to years:

- The **anniversary affect** that requires calendar correlation across a year of logs.
- The **archive expansion rate** — the slow, steady accretion of the Zemo lineage project, which is the truest record of his interior life and which looks, on any given day, like nothing.
- The **flourish escalation** that requires an active operation to express itself.
- The **substitution of intimacy with Rogers for any other intimacy** — invisible until one notes, after a year, that no name in his correspondence and no face in his rooms occupies the cognitive real estate that a man across the ocean, who does not know he is being thought of every day, occupies without effort.

The day-to-day file is the chassis. The man is in the longitudinal data. He has built a life designed to be **legible at the surface and opaque underneath**, and the discipline with which he maintains the surface is itself the most diagnostic single fact about him.

— END SECTION —


## Relationships I — Family & Origin Bonds

# RELATIONSHIPS I — FAMILY & ORIGIN BONDS

*UATU Dossier, Subject: Helmut Julius Fritz Zemo. Section 4 of the Relational Index. Cross-reference: Psychological Workup §3 (attachment), §4 (etiology), §5 (core drives #1).*

The Zemo family is not, in the ordinary sense, a family. It is a **transgenerational project** organized around a name, a title, an enemy, and a series of laboratory notebooks. To map Helmut's family bonds is therefore to map his relationship to an *idea* that wears the masks of dead people. The living human Helmut has loved, in any developmentally normal sense of the word, is — on the available evidence — exactly zero people. The figures below are not exceptions; they are the precise components of the cage that produced the absence.

What a total-surveillance file must capture here is not warmth (there is none to record) but **frequency of invocation**: how often, in monitored speech, correspondence, monologue, and behavior, each of these figures appears. By that metric the household is loud. Heinrich is referenced, by direct name or pronoun, in something on the order of a third of Helmut's recorded political speech and nearly all of his recorded private speech under stress. Hilda is referenced almost never. The grandfather, Herbert, is referenced when costume requires. The ancestors are referenced as a class, not as persons. This asymmetry is itself the family portrait.

---

## 4.1 — HEINRICH ZEMO (FATHER, 12TH BARON, DECEASED)

**Status:** Deceased, c. 1965, South American jungle. Killed by Captain America in a confrontation involving a rockfall and a discharged disintegrator beam (Avengers #15). Body unrecovered intact; remains, such as they were, repatriated by family retainers and interred in the Zemo crypt on the Bavarian/Sokovian estate. Helmut, an adolescent at the time of death, did not attend the recovery. He attended the interment.

**History.** Heinrich was effectively absent from Helmut's day-to-day childhood — first because of the war, then because of his fugitive science career in South America, then because of his death. The cumulative paternal hours logged with the child are, in any honest accounting, very few; the cumulative *paternal mythology* logged with the child is total. Helmut was raised not by his father but by the household's continuous narration of his father — by tutors, retainers, the maternal void, and a small library of confiscated papers and photographs that the boy was permitted to read in supervised conditions from approximately age seven. He learned his father's handwriting before he learned his father's voice. He recognized his father's face in three photographs before he recognized it across a room.

**Dynamic, as it actually was.** The relationship Helmut had with the living Heinrich was thin, formal, and conducted largely through letters and brief visits. The relationship Helmut has with the *dead* Heinrich is one of the densest in the file. The dead father is the addressee of nearly all internal monologue, the implicit audience of nearly all strategic theatre, the standard against which every act is measured. When Helmut wins, he wins **for** Heinrich. When he loses, he loses **before** Heinrich. The dead father has, in this sense, never died; he has merely become the camera.

**Dynamic, as Helmut narrates it.** Reverent. Unbroken. Heinrich is, in spoken record, "*mein Vater*" pronounced with a soft fricative and a half-beat pause that does not appear before any other noun in his speech. He is described variously as a man "ahead of his time," "the last serious scientist of the old continent," "a Zemo who understood the work." Helmut does not, in any monitored speech, use the words *Nazi*, *war criminal*, or *collaborator* in proximity to his father's name. The avoidance is not nervous; it is structural. The word *Heinrich* itself does not occur in his speech. It is always *mein Vater* or *the Baron* or, in formal contexts, *the twelfth*.

**Dynamic, as the evidence requires.** Helmut, on every available indicator, knows perfectly well what Heinrich was. He has read the papers. He has read the indictments. He has Citizen V'd himself into his own *grandfather's* identity precisely because the father's identity is unwearable. The Reaction Formation diagnosis in §3 is built on this: a man who genuinely revered his father's politics would not need to costume himself as his father's enemy to feel competent. The reverence is therefore *defensive* — a refusal to let the father be small. Helmut can survive having a *villain* for a father. He cannot survive having a *fool* for a father. The mythology is load-bearing.

**The mimetic injury (Captain America #168).** When Helmut, age approximately mid-twenties, attempts to drown Rogers in Adhesive X — the specific compound that fused Heinrich's mask to Heinrich's face — and instead falls in himself, the result is not merely a disfigurement. It is the **literalization of identification**. He emerged from that vat *wearing his father's wound*. Every subsequent hood is a continuation of that emergence. Surveillance note: in all canonical depictions of Helmut removing or being forced out of his hood, the first physical gesture of the bare-faced moment is a hand brought toward the face — never to cover it, but to *touch* it, as if confirming the topography is still there. He is checking for the father.

**Evolution across decades.** The relationship with Heinrich has *deepened* with time, not faded, which is the inverse of normal mourning. By the Born Better arc (Gage/Diggle) Helmut has gone backward through the bloodline and found a procession of monsters of which Heinrich is merely the most recent. He emerges from this research with a position that is, by his own standards, radical: that his father was wrong about the *means* but right about the *necessity*. This is the closest thing to paternal criticism Helmut has ever produced. He has had to walk back through six centuries of corpses to reach the modest sentence *my father was not the best Zemo*. He still cannot say *my father was bad*.

**Trust/safety vector.** Inapplicable in the standard sense (Heinrich is dead). In the operational sense: Heinrich is the **only entity in the file Helmut trusts unconditionally**, and the trust is in a memory he largely constructed.

**Failure mode.** Any framing that forces Helmut to evaluate Heinrich *as a man* rather than *as a Zemo* produces immediate cognitive narrowing. Interrogators who attempt this directly are dismissed or mocked; interrogators who approach it laterally (via the grandfather, via the lineage as a whole, via Roger Aubrey) produce measurable affect — pulse, breath, the slight tightening of the gloved hand on the pommel of the sword. He does not break. He does *constrict*.

**Leverage.** High but unreliable. Naming Heinrich destabilizes him; *humiliating* Heinrich (forcing comparison to a more competent Nazi scientist, e.g., Strucker; or to the grandfather; or to Rogers's own father figures) destabilizes him further. The risk in deploying this lever is that the destabilization translates not to compliance but to **escalation** — he becomes more dangerous, not more pliable, when the father is touched. A skilled operator uses Heinrich-leverage to *predict* Helmut's next move, not to extract behavior from him.

---

## 4.2 — HILDA ZEMO (MOTHER, BARONESS, DECEASED)

**Status:** Deceased. Date and cause inconsistent across canon and effectively unrecorded in Helmut's own speech. Functionally: gone before formative memory or gone so early in formative memory as to be indistinguishable from never. Buried, per family practice, in the estate crypt; her name appears on the stone in smaller incision than her husband's.

**History.** There is, in the entire recorded life of Helmut Zemo, no anecdote about his mother. No remembered phrase, no remembered scent, no remembered room. The household, by all reconstructions, continued in her absence without restructuring — the staff that raised the boy was the staff that would have raised the boy in any case. She left no visible hole because the architecture around her never integrated her load-bearing.

**Dynamic.** The diagnostic content here is the **silence itself**. A dismissive-avoidant attachment style, as noted in §3, does not narrate the missing caregiver; it organizes life around not needing one. Helmut's near-total non-reference to Hilda is therefore not evidence of *forgetting* (he forgets nothing) but of *not requiring*. He has built a self that does not have a mother-shaped vacancy because the self was assembled after the vacancy was already there. He does not miss what he never had to use.

**Indirect traces.** A surveillance file must catalogue what is conspicuous by absence. Helmut has no women in his life he treats as maternal — no older female advisor, no matriarch ally, no nostalgic relationship with any female figure of his childhood (nurse, governess, cook). His relations with women in adulthood are uniformly horizontal-instrumental: Moonstone, Songbird, the various brief liaisons. He does not idealize women. He does not denigrate them with the specific heat of misogynists who are working out a mother problem. He treats them, with absolute consistency, *as he treats men of equivalent rank* — which is, in a man of his class and century, itself a tell. The mother-frame is not damaged in him; it is **uninstalled.**

**Evolution.** None recordable. She is the only family member whose status in his inner life appears not to have changed across fifty years of canon. Everyone else has moved (Heinrich deepened, the ancestors clarified, the grandfather acquired strategic utility); Hilda is exactly where she was.

**Trust/safety vector.** Null.

**Failure mode.** There is one and it is interesting. Because Helmut has built no defenses *around* the mother (there being nothing to defend), any operator who can manufacture a *plausible* maternal figure — a woman, in particular, who reads as protective, competent, and not-sexual toward him — produces in him not affection but a quality of **discomforted attention** that he does not display elsewhere. He does not know the script. He improvises poorly. Across the canonical record this is rare (Helmut avoids such women, possibly preconsciously) but it occurs. He becomes formal in a way that is *more* formal than his baseline formality, which is the giveaway: the formality is now load-bearing, not ornamental.

**Leverage.** Low to moderate, indirect. Direct invocation of Hilda by name produces nothing — there is no associative network to fire. *Constructed* maternal pressure (the type of figure, not the name) produces measurable, low-grade destabilization that does not escalate to violence. It is one of the few levers in this file that *softens* rather than *sharpens* him. Of strategic interest precisely for that reason.

---

## 4.3 — HERBERT ZEMO (GRANDFATHER, 11TH BARON, DECEASED)

**Status:** Deceased before Helmut's birth or in earliest infancy. A WWI-era figure, known to Helmut entirely as a portrait, a set of dueling scars described in family lore, and a service record. In the Aubrey-line variant of the Citizen V mythology that Helmut later appropriates, an alternate or parallel figure (Roger Aubrey, the British Citizen V) overlaps in symbolic territory; in the Zemo household's own oral history, Herbert is positioned as the "*last* honorable Baron" — the man before Heinrich whose ledger is held to be clean.

**History.** Helmut never met him. The grandfather is therefore an even purer mythological object than the father — there is not even a thin layer of memory to contend with. He is whatever the household says he is, and the household says he was a soldier, a duellist, a man of the old code.

**Dynamic.** Operationally, Herbert serves Helmut as a **moral alibi within the lineage**. When Helmut needs to claim Zemo virtue without claiming Nazi virtue, he reaches past Heinrich to Herbert. The Citizen V impersonation in the Thunderbolts founding is the cleanest example of this: he wears, functionally, the grandfather's politics (or a version of them) to do the father's work. The grandfather is the *acceptable* Zemo, and Helmut returns to him whenever he needs the costume of acceptability.

**The diagnostic gesture.** Note that when Helmut needs to *be* a hero, he becomes the grandfather. When he needs to *avenge*, he becomes the father. The grandfather is the daylight identity; the father is the nighttime identity. The man underneath is the **inheritor who has not chosen which Zemo to be**, and this oscillation — Citizen V by morning, Baron Zemo by midnight — is not a Jekyll/Hyde dissociation. It is a perfectly conscious *rotation of masks within a single self-concept*. Helmut knows both are his.

**Evolution.** Herbert's utility has *risen* over Helmut's career. In youth, the grandfather was a portrait. By the Thunderbolts era, the grandfather was a costume. By the Born Better era, the grandfather was the proof-of-concept that the bloodline *could* produce something other than monstrosity. The grandfather is, by middle age, Helmut's preferred ancestor — a fact he has not articulated in plain speech because to articulate it would be to demote Heinrich.

**Trust/safety vector.** Inapplicable; symbolic only. Functionally, Helmut "trusts" the grandfather to confer legitimacy on actions taken in his name, which is to say Helmut trusts his own appropriation of him.

**Failure mode.** The Citizen V identity is the failure mode. He stole it (or a version of it) and the *legitimate holders of the V-Battalion lineage know it*. Any contact with the V-Battalion, with Roger Aubrey, or with the historical authenticity of the WWI/WWII Citizen V is a structural threat to one of Helmut's two operating costumes. He cannot simply discard the costume — it is the more important of the two — so he must defend it, and defending it forces him onto terrain (legitimacy, lineage, *who is the real Citizen V*) where his other half (the avenger of Heinrich) cannot help him.

**Leverage.** Moderate. The grandfather can be invoked to *constrain* Helmut into honorable conduct — he will fight by certain rules if he is operating in the Citizen V frame, and an operator who can keep him inside that frame can borrow those rules. Conversely, an operator who can *evict* him from the Citizen V frame (force him into the Baron Zemo frame in a moment when Citizen V was tactically required) inflicts a real cost.

---

## 4.4 — THE BLOODLINE (ANCESTORS, MEDIEVAL → MODERN)

**Status:** A class, not persons. Twelve preceding Barons, with collateral relations, retainers, and a documented genealogy back to (variously) the Crusades or the early Holy Roman period. The Zemo crypt holds most of them. The Zemo library holds their papers.

**History.** Helmut's research into the bloodline is *unusually deep* for a man of his pragmatic disposition. The Born Better arc is the public record of an inquiry he had clearly been conducting for years before it surfaced in plot. He has read the journals. He has reconstructed the campaigns. He knows which Baron poisoned which cousin, which one tortured which peasant uprising, which one collaborated with which occupying power. He treats the family record as a **case file** and himself as the investigator.

**Dynamic.** What he found, he has stated plainly (in the rare moments he states such things plainly): the Zemos have been, with negligible exceptions, terrible men. Not flawed men, not complicated men — *terrible*. His response to this discovery is the most psychologically revealing single act in his entire biography. He did not repudiate the line. He did not change his name. He did not seek a new tradition to be the first inheritor of. He chose to **continue the line with adjustment** — to be the Zemo who finally redirects the family's documented competence-for-cruelty toward an end he can call *order*.

This is the master diagnostic for his self-concept. A man capable of stepping outside the lineage frame would have stepped. A man for whom the lineage *is the only available frame* must instead reform it from within. Helmut is the second man. He cannot conceive of being not-a-Zemo. The only available moves are *better Zemo* or *worse Zemo*, and Born Better is his attempt at the first.

**Evolution.** Pre-Born Better, the ancestors were ambient — a portrait gallery he walked past. Post-Born Better, they are *interlocutors*. He has spent serious time, by his own oblique admission, in something like internal argument with the worst of them. This is not occultism; it is the cognitive activity of a man for whom the dead are the only peers he respects.

**Trust/safety vector.** Inapplicable.

**Failure mode.** The ancestors are the *substrate* of the failure mode that runs the whole file. As long as Helmut is operating inside the lineage frame, he cannot quit. He cannot retire. He cannot accept a clean defeat. Every loss is a loss *in the family ledger*, which is a ledger he is responsible for closing in the black. The bloodline is the reason he keeps standing up.

**Leverage.** Two contradictory levers. (a) Threats to the *line* (extinction of the name, defilement of the crypt, publication of the worst documents) produce immediate, escalated response — among the most reliable provocations in the file. (b) Conversely, *fatigue* of the line (the suggestion, gently introduced, that he has *already done enough* for the Zemos, that the ledger is balanced, that he may now rest) produces something rarer and more interesting: a brief, observable hesitation. He has been seen to take this question seriously and then to dismiss it. The dismissal is fast but not instant. The interval is the lever.

---

## 4.5 — CHILDREN

**Status:** None on canonical record. No acknowledged offspring, legitimate or otherwise. No documented attempt to produce an heir. No reported fertility issue; the absence appears deliberate.

**Dynamic.** This is, for a man whose master drive is the vindication of a *lineage*, the single most psychologically peculiar fact in the file. A Zemo without a son is the Zemo who ends the line. He has had decades, resources, opportunity, and a recurring stated commitment to the name. He has produced no successor.

**Interpretation.** Three readings, in order of evidential weight.

*First*: he believes the line ends best with its most accomplished member. To produce a son would be to subordinate his own claim to the lineage's culminating act; the son would have to surpass him to justify the continuation, and Helmut cannot model the existence of a Zemo who surpasses him. The line ends with him because *he is the apex*, and producing an heir would dilute the apex.

*Second*: the Born Better discovery has had a quiet consequence. Having confirmed that the Zemos are, on the historical record, monstrous, he cannot in good faith assign the burden to another consciousness. To father a Zemo is to sentence a child to the cage Helmut himself is in. The non-production of an heir is, on this reading, the closest thing to an *ethical* act in his entire biography — and it is unspoken, because to speak it would be to admit the cage.

*Third*: he has no interpersonal architecture for the necessary preliminaries. Romantic intimacy is uniformly transactional; the prospect of a co-parent is alien. He simply has not arranged the conditions.

The three readings are not exclusive. The first is the one he would, if asked, half-articulate. The second is the one he would deny. The third is the one he would not notice.

**Trust/safety vector.** Inapplicable.

**Failure mode.** The childlessness is itself a slow-burning structural failure. A mission organized around *vindicating a lineage that ends with the mission's executor* is logically self-cancelling. He is the last move in a game he is playing to win. He has not, on the available evidence, looked at this directly.

**Leverage.** Low and dangerous. The childlessness is a wound he does not know is a wound. An operator who names it risks producing not destabilization but **clarification** — forcing him to face the contradiction may simplify his motives rather than complicate them, and a simplified Helmut is a more effective Helmut. This lever should not be pulled by anyone who wants him slowed down.

---

## 4.6 — COLLATERAL KIN AND THE EXTENDED HOUSE

**Status:** A small number of distant cousins, a network of family retainers (some multigenerational in service to the house), the legal apparatus that has managed the estate through wars, occupations, and successive collapses of the political order around it.

**Dynamic.** Helmut maintains the estate. He maintains the staff. He maintains the legal continuity of the title in whatever jurisdictions still recognize it. He is a *competent landlord* and a *correct employer*. Retainers are paid, pensioned, and protected; their children are educated at his expense where the family tradition calls for it. This is not warmth. It is **noblesse oblige** executed to specification, and it is one of the few areas in his life where his behavior is reliably benign.

**Diagnostic.** The retainers are the only category of person to whom Helmut owes *unilateral obligation* in his own frame — they serve the house, the house serves them, the contract is older than any individual party to it. He honors it because the *house* requires it, not because he likes them. They are, accordingly, **safer around him than almost anyone else in the file**, including his own ideological allies.

**Trust/safety vector.** Asymmetric. He trusts the senior retainers in narrow operational matters (discretion, continuity, custody of the estate) absolutely. They do not trust him personally — they trust *the position he occupies*. Both parties understand this and prefer it to the alternative.

**Failure mode.** A retainer who attempts to address Helmut as a *person* rather than as the Baron breaches the contract on the retainer's side. Such breaches are handled coldly but without cruelty — dismissal, not violence. Helmut does not punish category errors; he corrects them.

**Leverage.** Substantial and underused by his adversaries. The estate, the retainers, and the legal continuity of the title are the *physical infrastructure* of the lineage-frame that organizes him. Disrupt the infrastructure and the frame becomes harder to maintain. No major operator has attempted this systematically, partly because it requires patience on a scale that matches his own and partly because the targets are civilians whom most of his enemies will not touch. The fact that *Helmut himself would touch them in the inverse case* is one of the asymmetries that has historically protected him.

---

## SECTION SYNTHESIS

The family file resolves to four operative truths.

**One.** Helmut has no living family bonds. Every figure in this section is either dead, mythological, hypothetical, or contractual. The absence of a single warm contemporary tie in the family register is not a gap in the dossier; it is the dossier's finding.

**Two.** The dead father is the most important person in his life and has been for half a century. Every major operational pattern in the file is downstream of the unresolved identification with Heinrich — the hood, the sword, the lineage obsession, the inability to convert symbolic victory into actual victory, the Cap fixation. To predict Helmut at any horizon longer than seventy-two hours, model Heinrich first.

**Three.** The mother's absence is the silent precondition. The dismissive-avoidant attachment style that allows him to operate without peer bonds, without intimacy, without grief that registers as grief, was installed by the Hilda-vacancy and has never been challen


## Relationships II — Allies, Chosen Family & Mentors

# RELATIONSHIPS II — ALLIES, CHOSEN FAMILY & MENTORS

## Preamble: The Category Problem

A standard relational dossier presumes the subject has allies, friends, chosen family, and mentors as distinct categories. Subject HELMUT ZEMO does not. The taxonomy below is preserved for structural completeness, but the analytic finding it documents is the **near-total absence of non-instrumental bonds** across a fifty-year operational record. Subject does not maintain friendships. He maintains *staffing*. He does not adopt; he *retains*. Mentorship is one-way and downward, never received. What follows is therefore less a record of intimacies than a catalog of the **shapes that warmth would take if subject were capable of it** — the people who occupied, however briefly, the functional sockets where allies, kin, and teachers would belong in another man's life. Several of these subjects appear elsewhere in the file as enemies; that they appear *here* at all is the data point. He has, on more than one occasion, been almost-loved by someone he was using. The almost is the architecture.

---

## 1. HEINRICH ZEMO (Father — Posthumous Mentor / Phantom Limb)

The defining relationship of subject's life is with a man he barely knew alive and has not stopped consulting since 1965.

**History.** Heinrich Zemo, 12th Baron, Nazi scientist, dies in a South American jungle when subject is a child. The household subject is raised inside is not a household; it is a **shrine with staff**. Tutors, family retainers, the long-serving estate steward (canonical references to a Bavarian housekeeper-figure who effectively raises Helmut through adolescence; subject never names her in any recorded statement, which is the data point) — all organized around the maintenance of paternal mythology. Subject's exposure to actual Heinrich is reconstructive: lab notebooks, photographs, recorded lectures, third-party hagiography, a sealed wing of the estate containing original Adhesive X apparatus that subject visits ritually from age eleven onward (inferable from the precision with which he later replicates the compound).

**Dynamics.** The father is the only figure in subject's interior life granted unqualified positive valence. He is consulted in moments of decision — not literally, but as a *standard*: would Heinrich do this, would Heinrich approve this, is this worthy of the name. The internalized Heinrich is **less a person than a regulatory function**, the superego dressed in a lab coat and a swastika. Diagnostically, this is the source of subject's unusual moral self-confidence: he has an authority to defer to, and that authority never argues back.

**Evolution.** Across fifty years the relationship slowly cracks. Phoenix-era Helmut (1973) consults the father wholly — the choice of Adhesive X is *Heinrich's weapon*, used in *Heinrich's manner*, against *Heinrich's enemy*.
