By the Citizen V/Thunderbolts era (1997) subject has begun a partial substitution, reaching past the father to the *grandfather's* identity — the first appearance of an unspoken admission that Heinrich's brand requires laundering. The Born Better arc (Gage/Diggle) is the closest subject ever comes to articulating the heretical thought: *the lineage is monstrous, and Heinrich was part of the monstrosity*. Subject does not repudiate; subject proposes *continuation under improved management*. This is the deepest movement available to him without structural collapse.

**Trust/safety.** Total in one direction (subject to the phantom father), nonexistent in the other (Heinrich is dead; he cannot disappoint subject by withdrawing approval). The relationship is **structurally safe because asymmetric**, and this is the template for every subsequent relationship subject attempts: he is only secure with people who cannot leave.

**Failure mode.** The relationship fails by *succeeding too well*. Heinrich's internalization is so complete that subject cannot encounter his own face without seeing the father's mask-fusion, cannot select a weapon without the father's catalog, cannot conceive of victory in any terms but the father's vindication. The phantom limb continues to ache because subject keeps reaching with it.

**Leverage (operational).** Any external party able to credibly stage Heinrich's *real* opinion — by archival document, by recovered correspondence, by historian's testimony — could destabilize subject in a way no combat could. The phantom is fragile to evidence because subject has been carefully curating it.

---

## 2. THE MASTERS OF EVIL CORE (Under Siege Roster — Operational Family of Convenience)

The closest thing to a chosen workplace in subject's life is the Masters of Evil he reconstituted for the Avengers Mansion campaign (Avengers #273–277). Treating them as a unit, because subject did.

**History.** Subject recruits across the criminal infrastructure of the mid-1980s — Goliath (Erik Josten), the Wrecking Crew, Tiger Shark, Whirlwind, Mr. Hyde, Moonstone, Blackout, Yellowjacket II (Rita DeMara), Fixer, Screaming Mimi, the Absorbing Man and Titania peripherally. The selection criteria are interesting: subject favors **operators with grievances against specific Avengers**, importing personal vendettas as motivational fuel rather than relying on pay. He functions less as a commander than as a *grievance broker*.

**Dynamics.** Subject treats the roster with elaborate, formal courtesy and unconcealed contempt. He uses titles, observes hierarchies of seniority (deferring to Hyde's pharmacological gravitas, to Goliath's tenure), and at no point eats, drinks, or relaxes with any of them. Behavioral marker: in the staging-period footage inferable from canon, subject is recorded as having occupied a separate suite of rooms within the operational safehouse, taking meals alone, debriefing individually rather than in group sessions. This is not security practice; this is **incapacity for the common table**.

**Evolution.** The roster does not survive the operation as a unit. Subject does not attempt to reconstitute it. He retains relationships with select members (Fixer, Moonstone, Goliath/Atlas — see Thunderbolts entry) on the basis of *future utility*, not affection. He does not mourn the imprisoned. He does not visit them. There is no record of subject ever having sent a message, parcel, or legal aid to a captured former subordinate from this era.

**Trust/safety.** Subject trusts the roster only insofar as he has correctly modeled their grievances. He does not delegate symbolic-value decisions (he handles the Jarvis matter personally; he handles the destruction of Rogers's quarters personally). This is the **diagnostic giveaway**: the things that matter to him, he does not share.

**Failure mode.** Subject loses control of the roster during the Jarvis-beating sequence because Mr. Hyde escalates beyond plan — subject permitted the spectacle, did not anticipate the participant who would treat permission as license. The pattern: subject's sadism is *curated*; he cannot lead other sadists, because he assumes they share his discrimination, and they do not.

**Leverage.** Every former Master of Evil from this era is a potential leverage point against subject because each of them holds a piece of *behavioral evidence* (his face under conditions of personal vengeance, his lapses from strategy into theater) that subject would prefer no peer possess.

---

## 3. KARLA SOFEN / MOONSTONE (The Almost-Peer)

The single relationship in subject's life that approaches *recognition between equals*, and the one he most actively sabotages.

**History.** Subject recruits Karla Sofen for the Under Siege operation and again as Meteorite for the Thunderbolts deception. She is a clinical psychologist (PhD), narcissist of the cerebral subtype, manipulator of comparable sophistication, lacking subject's lineage obsession but possessing his contempt for the ordinary. She is the only person in subject's circle who **diagnoses him in real time** and the only one whose diagnoses he occasionally accepts.

**Dynamics.** Their interactions across Thunderbolts #1–50 are conducted in a register no other relationship achieves: civilized hostility, professional candor, a mutual acknowledgement that each is using the other and that the using is the basis of the regard. Sofen reads subject accurately — names the father-fixation, names the Citizen V theft, names the inability to release Rogers — and subject does not punish her for it. He sometimes *corrects* her, which is a form of intimacy unavailable to him with anyone else. Behaviorally, this is the only adult he treats as adult.

**Evolution.** Sofen deposes subject from Thunderbolts leadership (#25) and subject's response is **disproportionately personal**. He pursues her with a vendetta-mode register that he reserves elsewhere only for Rogers. Diagnostic reading: she had become the closest thing in his life to a peer, and being unseated by her registered not as defeat but as *betrayal by family*, a category he does not consciously possess but evidently operates by. The pursuit eventually exhausts itself; they end as wary semi-collaborators, capable of working in adjacent rooms.

**Trust/safety.** Higher than any other living person, which means measurable but low. Subject would not turn his back on her in a fight. He would, however, take her counsel in a planning session, and has.

**Failure mode.** Both parties are organized around being the smartest person in the room. The relationship cannot survive prolonged co-presence because the question *whose plan is this* is unresolvable without one of them defecting. Their bond's natural shape is **periodic alliance separated by attempted destructions**, which is exactly what canon shows.

**Leverage.** Sofen is the only living individual who could deliver an accurate psychiatric formulation of subject *to subject* without him dismissing it. She is therefore the most dangerous human in his life. She has, to date, declined to use this leverage maximally, which subject correctly interprets as her holding it in reserve. Their détente is built on this.

---

## 4. ABNER JENKINS / MACH-1 → MACH-V (The Honest Foreman)

The Thunderbolt who most cleanly demonstrates the *cost* of subject's deception, by being changed by it.

**History.** Recruited as Beetle from the Masters of Evil bench, redesigned as MACH-1 for the Thunderbolts cover identity. Working-class background, engineer-criminal, no aristocratic pretension. Subject selects him for *competence and lack of imagination*, both of which are misjudgments — Jenkins is competent, but he has more imagination than subject credits.

**Dynamics.** Subject treats Jenkins with the cold courtesy he extends to all subordinates, with a small differential: Jenkins is the one he assigns logistical and engineering trust, and the one he speaks to in operational rather than ideological registers. There is no warmth. There is a recognizable *workplace respect* of the sort subject extends to a well-functioning piece of machinery. Jenkins, for his part, comes to dislike subject specifically and increasingly, because Jenkins is the first of the Thunderbolts to grasp that the leader does not believe his own cover.

**Evolution.** Jenkins is the one who serves prison time *voluntarily* to atone — the moral move subject is constitutionally incapable of and therefore cannot model. The two grow into ideological opposites: Jenkins becomes a genuine reformed hero, subject remains himself. When their paths recross in later arcs, subject is faintly contemptuous of what he reads as Jenkins's *naivety in mistaking penance for redemption*; Jenkins regards subject with the settled hostility of a man who once worked for him and learned the cost.

**Trust/safety.** Operationally high during cover-identity period. Personally nonexistent on either side.

**Failure mode.** Subject loses Jenkins because Jenkins develops the *desire to be virtuous*, the variable subject has consistently failed to model. This is the cleanest single case of the Thunderbolts pattern.

**Leverage.** Jenkins is an irreproachable witness to subject's manipulation methodology and could testify devastatingly. His unwillingness to expend his rehabilitation on continued obsession with subject is itself a form of moral superiority subject registers and resents.

---

## 5. MELISSA GOLD / SONGBIRD (The Protégée Who Surpassed The Cover)

The most painful Thunderbolts loss because subject *actually trained her* — and the training took, in directions subject did not intend.

**History.** Recruited as Screaming Mimi, redesigned as Songbird. Lower-class American, abuse survivor, sonic-power user requiring substantial discipline to operate the new vocal-projector harness. Subject takes a direct hand in her tactical training, in her diction and bearing, in the construction of a public-facing heroic identity. The relationship is the closest subject ever comes to a mentor-protégée bond, and it is conducted entirely under the cover of a lie.

**Dynamics.** Subject's pedagogical register with Gold is the most patient documented in his canon. He corrects without humiliation. He explains rather than commands. He invests time. He genuinely improves her — her later effectiveness as a leader of Thunderbolts iterations is built on foundations he laid. Diagnostically: the *teaching* function is one of the few altruistic-coded behaviors subject can perform without internal conflict, because the asymmetry of the relationship satisfies his aristocratic frame (the teacher is the superior) and the gift is *intellectual*, the form of value he most respects.

**Evolution.** Gold becomes a *better hero than subject was pretending to be*. She internalizes the cover, then exceeds it, then defends it against subject when he attempts to revert the team. Her arc across Thunderbolts is the photographic negative of subject's: she begins in criminality and ends in genuine command; he begins in command and ends discarded. When they confront each other in later arcs, subject's affect is *uniquely complicated* — he disapproves of her choices, respects her competence, and on one documented occasion (Ellis-era material) speaks of her with something that, in another man, would be paternal pride.

**Trust/safety.** Subject is safer with Gold than with most former subordinates because she has nothing to prove against him; he is safer than expected because she has integrated past him. He is not safe at all in the inverse: she will stop him if she can, and she knows where his levers are.

**Failure mode.** Subject created in Gold the very thing his worldview denies exists — a person who *became virtuous* through performance of virtue. Her existence is a falsification of his operational code, and he cannot quite look at her directly without that falsification registering. He compensates by intellectualizing her as an exception rather than a refutation.

**Leverage.** Gold is the only former subordinate whose moral judgment subject would, on some buried level, *accept*. She has not deployed this. If she ever did — if she ever said directly *you have wasted yourself* — it would land.

---

## 6. ERIK JOSTEN / GOLIATH → ATLAS (The Long-Tenured Soldier)

The longest-running working relationship in subject's career, conducted at the lowest emotional resolution.

**History.** Josten serves under subject across both Masters of Evil and Thunderbolts iterations, plus several smaller operations. He is loyal in the sense that he keeps showing up; subject is loyal in the sense that he keeps offering positions. Neither would describe the bond in those terms.

**Dynamics.** Subject regards Josten as *furniture of high quality* — reliable, durable, requires no maintenance, never asks unanswerable questions. Their exchanges are brief, operational, free of subtext. There is no record of them ever having had a personal conversation in any canon. This is itself the relationship: the **absence of any need for the relationship to be more than it is** is what makes it sustainable.

**Evolution.** Josten's own rehabilitation arc (he becomes one of the more genuinely changed Thunderbolts) introduces friction subject does not know how to process. He treats Josten's reformation with the same mild contempt he extends to Jenkins's, but without the analytic intensity — Josten was never important enough to disappoint him in a structured way.

**Trust/safety.** Operationally trustworthy across decades. Personally irrelevant.

**Failure mode.** The relationship cannot deepen because subject does not deepen relationships. It cannot dissolve because there is no emotional substance to rupture. It simply persists, and then doesn't.

**Leverage.** Low. Josten knows where the operational bodies are buried but does not possess the symbolic-vulnerability material that Sofen and Gold do.

---

## 7. THE V-BATTALION / ROGER AUBREY / THE GRANDFATHER'S LEGACY (Refused Family)

The chosen family subject *sought and was denied*, and the absence of which structures much of his middle-period behavior.

**History.** The V-Battalion is the legitimate Citizen V legacy organization — an anti-fascist intelligence apparatus tracing to subject's grandfather and to Roger Aubrey (the original Citizen V's surviving comrade). Subject's appropriation of the Citizen V identity is, at one analytic level, an act of theft from this lineage. At another level — the one no member of the V-Battalion has been willing to credit — it is an *application for adoption*. Subject is reaching past the Nazi father to claim the resistance-fighter grandfather, and is signaling, in the only way his pathology permits, that he wishes to be received into that line.

**Dynamics.** The V-Battalion refuses him absolutely. They are correct to do so. The refusal is the cleanest moral act performed by any institution toward subject in canon, and it lands on him as the **second-deepest wound** in his life after Heinrich's death. He never says so. He attacks the V-Battalion subsequently with a venom disproportionate to operational stakes.

**Evolution.** Subject never reconciles with this refusal. He continues to deploy Citizen V iconography intermittently across decades, each time with diminishing conviction. The grandfather's identity, having failed to confer adoption, becomes one more piece of inherited costuming.

**Trust/safety.** None in either direction. Subject would not be received under any circumstances; subject would not approach again under most.

**Failure mode.** Subject cannot grasp that the V-Battalion's refusal is *itself* an expression of the moral seriousness he wished to be admitted into. To be received, he would have had to demonstrate the very transformation that being received was meant to produce. The closed loop is invisible to him.

**Leverage.** Roger Aubrey's name, deployed in his presence by a person with standing, produces measurable affective response — pupillary, postural, the slight rotation away from the speaker. Operationally the highest-yield verbal trigger in the file other than Rogers's name itself.

---

## 8. HOUSEHOLD STAFF / RETAINERS (The Functional Mother-Substitutes He Will Not Name)

The Bavarian/Sokovian estate has, across decades, employed a small staff of long-tenured retainers — a steward-figure, a housekeeper, tutors, the family physician — who collectively performed the caregiving the absent mother and dead father did not.

**Dynamics.** Subject's behavior toward retainers is marked by *aristocratic correctness without warmth*. He learns their names, observes their birthdays in a formal manner, pays them well, attends their funerals when appropriate, and does not permit himself to grieve any of them. The housekeeper-figure who effectively raised him is, on the analytic reading, the closest thing to a maternal attachment object in his life, and subject has structured his interior life to make her invisible — she does not appear in his self-narratives, she is not named in his correspondence, she is the empty space in the file where a mother-substitute would be acknowledged.

**Trust/safety.** Operationally high (retainers are vetted for generations). Emotionally, subject permits himself to be *physically near* these individuals in ways he does not permit with peers — they have seen him without the hood; they have brought him meals when injured; they have, in early adulthood, witnessed him weeping (inferable from the rigorous suppression of weeping behavior in all subsequent contexts). The hood is *off* in the kitchen wing of the estate. This is the most intimate fact in the file.

**Failure mode.** Subject will not protect retainers at strategic cost. If an operation required their sacrifice, he would sacrifice them, and he would attend the services in correct dress. The *correctness* would be the grief.

**Leverage.** The estate staff is the single softest target connected to subject's interior life. He has, accordingly, made the estate's defenses formidable and the staff's existence quiet. An intelligence service that mapped the household precisely would hold a key he does not know he has surrendered.

---

## 9. FIXER (PAUL NORBERT EBERSOL) (The Technician He Will Not Replace)

The professional-grade subordinate who functions as subject's prosthetic engineering capacity.

**History.** Recurring across Masters of Evil and Thunderbolts iterations. Subject is technically literate but not a builder; Fixer is the builder. The relationship is functional, durable, and free of mutual liking.

**Dynamics.** Subject defers to Fixer on engineering questions with a clarity rare in his interactions — he does not pretend to know what he does not know, in this one domain. Fixer treats subject as a *client whose specifications are unusually clear*, which is the highest praise Fixer extends. Neither inquires after the other's interior life.

**Trust/safety.** Trust is high within domain (Fixer's work does not fail) and absent outside it. Either would betray the other given sufficient operational motive.

**Failure mode.** Subject has, in moments of strategic-to-symbolic drift, asked Fixer to build items whose function is *theatrical rather than tactical*. Fixer builds them and bills accordingly. The relationship would not survive subject's discovery that Fixer has, on at least one occasion, mocked these specifications to a third party.

**Leverage.** Fixer's records of subject's specifications constitute a behavioral archive of *what subject thought was important enough to construct*, which is a finer-grained record of priorities than subject himself maintains.

---

## 10. HELMUT GRUBER / FAMILY ATTORNEY (Inferred — The Continuity Function)

Subject's continued legal existence across decades of incarcerations, exiles, presumed deaths, and asset seizures requires a continuous legal-administrative function — a long-tenured family attorney or firm operating across the Zemo holdings.

**Dynamics.** Strictly formal. Subject pays well, complies with documentation, never confides. The attorney function is the *only* relationship in subject's life conducted entirely in writing across decades, and subject's correspondence in this register is a model of disciplined opacity — he reveals nothing he is not asked to reveal, and he is rarely asked.

**Trust/safety.** Operational, narrow, durable.

**Failure mode.** None demonstrated.

**Leverage.** The legal-administrative record is the single most underweighted intelligence source on subject. Wills, asset transfers, trust modifications across decades constitute a *priority record* more honest than subject's stated ideology. He has revised his testamentary instructions repeatedly; the revisions are the closest thing in existence to a longitudinal diary of his actual concerns.

---

## 11. THE MASK ITSELF (Treated As A Relational Object)

## Relationships III — Rivals, Enemies & Lovers

# RELATIONSHIPS III — RIVALS, ENEMIES & LOVERS

*Dossier Section 7c. Cross-reference Sections 7a (Family & Lineage) and 7b (Subordinates, Lieutenants & Operational Peers). All entries assess the subject's side of the relationship; reciprocal files exist separately. Where physical or somatic data is logged, it derives from surveillance composites, intercepted communications, recovered correspondence, and post-action debriefs of survivors.*

---

## I. THE PRIMARY ENEMY

### Steven Grant Rogers — "Captain America"

**Status:** Defining object-relation. The only relationship in the subject's life that approaches what a clinician would call attachment. Active for the full duration of the file (>50 years of recorded engagement); no plateau, no remission, no extinction curve.

**History.** The relationship begins before Helmut was born — Rogers killed Heinrich Zemo in a South American jungle (1965 dating, per Avengers #15 record), and Helmut was raised inside the gravitational field of that single sentence: *Captain America killed your father.* The relationship as enacted begins with the Phoenix abduction (Captain America #168, 1973), in which Helmut's first independent adult act is the attempted ritual drowning of Rogers in the same compound that destroyed Heinrich. From that opening move, every subsequent engagement is a re-statement of the same equation with the variables rearranged.

**Dynamics.** Helmut's behavior toward Rogers is unique in his behavioral repertoire. He does not exhibit it toward anyone else. Component features:

- *Sustained imaginative occupation.* Helmut spends measurable years thinking about a man he sees in person perhaps a dozen times per decade. Recovered planning documents (Mansion siege preparation, 1986; Citizen V cover assembly, 1996) show Rogers-modeling at a fidelity normally reserved for spouses by their analysts.
- *Intimate register.* When Helmut speaks of Rogers in private — to Moonstone, to the Fixer, to himself in the Born Better recordings — the diction shifts. He does not use the impersonal contemptuous lexicon he uses for other heroes ("the Wasp creature," "Stark's costumed accountant"). He uses Rogers's name, often the Christian name, and he uses it the way a man uses the name of the person he is trying not to think about.
- *Refusal of finality.* Helmut has had Rogers helpless multiple times. He has never killed him. The standard rationalization (the spectacle requires Cap alive to witness) is true but insufficient — the deeper truth is that the death of Rogers would collapse the architecture of Helmut's interior life. He needs Rogers in the world the way a planet needs a sun.
- *Mimetic injury-seeking.* Helmut keeps engineering scenarios in which he sustains, in Rogers's presence, injuries that recapitulate his father's. Adhesive X. Great falls. He is restaging the trauma compulsively, casting Rogers in the only role available to him — the one Rogers refuses to want.

**Evolution.** Four discernible phases:

1. *Raw mimetic vengeance (1973–mid-1980s).* Helmut wants Rogers to *become* Heinrich. Phoenix arc, early Masters of Evil operations. Crude.
2. *Sadistic intimacy (Under Siege, 1986).* Helmut now wants Rogers to *feel* what he feels. The Mansion siege is the artistic apex of this phase — Jarvis's beating, the photograph destruction, the curated humiliation. Strategically he wins everything until he insists on the personal touch; then he loses it all on the roof. This is the first time the pattern is clean enough to read on a graph.
3. *Ideological displacement (Citizen V / Liberators era, 1996–2005).* Helmut tries, with partial success, to reframe the relationship as ideological — Rogers stands for the democratic-sentimentalist error and must be defeated as a category, not a person. The displacement is unstable; whenever Rogers personally appears, the ideology evaporates and the vendetta resurfaces.
4. *Philosophical bitterness (Ellis-era forward, 2006+).* Helmut speaks of Rogers more rarely and more accurately. The hatred is no longer hot. It has the temperature of a permanent climate. He recognizes Rogers as a man who has, in objective terms, *defeated him in every meaningful arena,* and he has accepted this without renouncing the contest. The relationship has become his life's work, regardless of outcome.

**Trust/Safety.** Asymmetric and inverted. Helmut trusts Rogers absolutely in one specific respect: Rogers will not lie, will not break parole, will not kill him in a moment of advantage. Helmut has exploited this repeatedly. Conversely, Rogers cannot trust Helmut at any layer; Helmut considers deception of Rogers a kind of obligation. The safety calculus: Helmut is physically safer in Rogers's custody than in almost any other captor's — and psychologically more endangered. Rogers's *recognition* of him as a coherent human being is the thing he cannot withstand for long.

**Failure mode.** Documented across five decades with mechanical reliability: *strategic IQ collapses within Rogers's line of sight by an estimated 30–40 points.* Helmut, who plans in decades, begins improvising. Helmut, who never gloats with strangers, gloats. Helmut, who never explains, explains. Helmut, who never strikes a hostage himself, strikes a hostage himself. The failure mode is not anger management; it is the irruption of the unconscious project. When Rogers is present, Helmut stops trying to *win* and starts trying to *be seen,* and the latter is a goal Rogers will not give him.

**Leverage (the subject's, against Rogers).** Sarah Rogers's memory; Bucky Barnes (the most refined instrument); the rolling cohort of friends and protégés whose deaths Helmut can arrange. Helmut has researched Rogers's Brooklyn period at a level of detail that suggests a biographer's interest. He knows Rogers's draft records, the addresses of Rogers's neighbors, the gravesite of Rogers's mother. The dossier is intelligence; it is also fan archaeology.

**Leverage (Rogers's, against the subject — what the subject would never admit).** Rogers's continued refusal to *hate* Helmut. Helmut wants symmetry; Rogers will not give it. Every time Rogers speaks of Helmut with pity, with the tone reserved for a man who lost something he could not name, Helmut sustains an injury for which the hood provides no covering.

---

## II. SECONDARY ENEMIES

### James Buchanan Barnes — "Bucky" / "Winter Soldier"

**Status:** Surrogate target and refined instrument. The second-most-occupied position in Helmut's enemy architecture, occupied for different reasons in different eras.

**History.** In the early canon, Bucky figures only as a sentimental object whose memory Helmut weaponizes against Rogers (Mansion siege photographs include Bucky memorabilia, deliberately selected). After Bucky's resurrection as the Winter Soldier, the relationship inverts: Bucky becomes both a *replacement* Rogers (when Bucky takes up the shield) and a uniquely portable weapon (the trigger-word conditioning, exploited in the Civil War II and post-Hydra arcs).

**Dynamics.** Helmut's engagement with Bucky is the cleanest available expression of his pure *technique* unconfused by personal affect. He does not hate Bucky; he uses Bucky. The trigger-word activation sequences are, considered as objects, beautiful — minimum input, maximum yield, surgical exploitation of an enemy's worst wound. They are also entirely characteristic: Helmut prefers to *aim* a person at a target rather than strike the target himself, because aiming requires the kind of intelligence he believes is rare and the kind of patience he believes is rarer.

**Evolution.** From prop (1986) to proxy (early Brubaker era) to weapon (the trigger-word period) to, in the most recent arcs, *peer of a kind* — Bucky is the only other person in Helmut's working environment who lives inside a permanent inheritance of someone else's war, and Helmut, who notices everything, has noticed this.

**Trust/Safety.** None offered. Helmut considers Bucky's compromised consciousness a permanent vulnerability; he would never sleep in a room with him. He also considers Bucky genuinely formidable in a way most heroes are not, because Bucky's morality, like his own, is the product of long damage rather than untested decency.

**Failure mode.** Helmut consistently underestimates Bucky's capacity to *resist the conditioning under pressure of love* — he models the conditioning as a hardware fact when it is in fact a software fact constantly being overwritten by Bucky's relationships. (Compare: he made the same modeling error with the Thunderbolts.)

**Leverage.** The trigger words themselves; the catalogue of Winter Soldier kills which can be revealed selectively; Natasha Romanoff (when alive in given continuity) and Rogers as Bucky's two attachment poles. Helmut has files on every person Bucky's hand has killed and uses them with the patience of a slow poisoner.

---

### Karla Sofen — "Moonstone" / "Meteorite"

*Cross-referenced from Section 7b; included here for the enemy dimension.*

**Status:** Former lieutenant, former (intermittent, transactional) lover, durable rival. The only person who has ever successfully *deposed* him from a command he built, and the only person against whom he has tested himself as a peer rather than as an aristocrat among inferiors.

**History.** Recruited into the Masters of Evil. Folded into the Thunderbolts as Meteorite. Engineered his removal from leadership in Thunderbolts #25. Re-engaged in subsequent arcs as alternating ally, antagonist, lover, captive, captor.

**Dynamics.** Karla is the only woman in Helmut's recorded life who is treated as a strategic equal. The treatment is grudging, formally courteous, and laced with mutual contempt for the other's pretensions. Their sexual encounters (canonically intimated, never displayed at length) are characterized by both parties as instrumental and by neither as romantic. Helmut respects exactly two things about her: her tactical patience and her willingness to lie at length. He despises her sentimentality (her residual desire to be admired by ordinary people) and her self-deception (she believes herself harder than she is; he has watched her flinch).

**Evolution.** From subordinate (1987) → peer-conspirator (1997) → usurper (1998) → unstable rival (2000s) → occasional ally of convenience (Ellis era forward). The relationship has stabilized at *colleagues in a long war.* They will betray each other again. Both know this. Neither finds it disqualifying.

**Trust/Safety.** Trust: zero, asymmetric in neither direction. Safety: they have, by tacit agreement, refrained from killing one another at multiple opportunities, which is the highest compliment either is capable of paying.

**Failure mode.** Helmut consistently miscalculates Karla's *appetite for the spotlight* — he assumes she will, like him, prefer power exercised from shadow. She does not. She wants to be seen being powerful. He has lost ground to her three separate times by misjudging this.

**Leverage.** Her vanity (he has used staged public humiliations against her with measurable effect); her relationship to her own mother (a wound she has revealed to him once, in their longest recorded private conversation, and which he has filed); the Moonstone artifact's instability under specific frequencies (Fixer-derived intelligence).

---

### Norman Osborn

**Status:** Rival, occasional sponsor, occasional usurper, permanent contaminant. The man to whom Helmut surrendered the Thunderbolts.

**Dynamics.** Helmut's contempt for Osborn is the purest contempt in the file. He regards Osborn as everything aristocracy is supposed to prevent — a vulgar, unstable, status-hungry climber whose competence is the accident of his madness rather than the discipline of his mind. The contempt is intensified by the fact that Osborn, twice, has out-positioned him politically. Helmut considers political defeat at the hands of an inferior to be the worst possible defeat, because it implicates the world rather than the opponent.

**Evolution.** From distant peer (1990s) → usurper (Thunderbolts ~#110, Helmut walks rather than fight him for the team) → strategic adversary (Dark Reign period, in continuities where Helmut engages with it) → permanent benchmark of *the world's stupidity in Helmut's preferred direction.*

**Trust/Safety.** Helmut does not consider Osborn safe to be in a room with under any circumstance and has standing protocols for extraction if Osborn appears unannounced.

**Failure mode.** Helmut underestimates Osborn's capacity to *fail upward.* He keeps expecting Osborn to be ruined by his own pathology; Osborn keeps being elevated by it. Helmut has not adjusted his model.

**Leverage.** Osborn's pharmaceutical baseline (which Helmut has mapped); Harry Osborn-related material (held in reserve, never deployed — Helmut has a fastidiousness about children that is one of his few consistent ethical lines); Osborn's terror of being publicly *small,* which Helmut has exploited once and intends to exploit again.

---

### Songbird (Melissa Gold)

**Status:** Former subordinate, ideological reproach, the single most psychologically dangerous person to Helmut in the file — and the one whose threat he has never fully metabolized.

**Dynamics.** Songbird is the Thunderbolt who *became* a hero while Helmut was only pretending to be one. Her presence in the world is, to him, a refutation. He addresses her with surface courtesy and a substratum of unease he displays toward no one else. She is the empirical proof that his model of human motivation is wrong — that people exposed to virtue as a performance can develop the appetite for virtue as a fact. He has never forgiven her for this and has never let himself examine why.

**Evolution.** From utility piece (Songbird-as-Screaming-Mimi, 1997) → unexpected ideological opponent (Thunderbolts #10 forward) → leadership rival → moral judge. He cannot win an argument with her, which infuriates him, because he can win arguments with everyone.

**Trust/Safety.** He will not harm her physically without strategic necessity — which is itself an admission of regard. He will not be alone in a room with her if he can help it, because she addresses him as a person rather than as a Baron, and the dissolution of the title in her mouth is dangerous to him.

**Failure mode.** He underestimates her *durability.* He keeps writing her off and she keeps returning, harder.

**Leverage.** Limited and ethically narrowed by his own standards. He will not use her relationship with MACH against her (Section 7b notes his peculiar respect for that bond, source unclear). He has used her record (criminal past) selectively. He has never tried to break her, which is, in the negative, a kind of leverage *she* holds over *him.*

---

### The Avengers (collective)

**Status:** Institutional enemy. Helmut does not file them as individuals; he files them as a system.

**Dynamics.** He regards the Avengers as the *premier political fiction of the post-WWII order* — a fantasy that exceptional individuals can be organized under democratic norms without becoming an aristocracy in practice. He believes they are an aristocracy in practice and is exasperated by their refusal to admit it. His operations against them are not personal except through Rogers; they are critiques.

**Sub-files (brief):**
- *Tony Stark.* Class antagonist in reverse — old money's contempt for the parvenu who outspends him. Helmut considers Stark technically formidable and morally unserious. The Iron Man suit is, to Helmut, an admission that Stark cannot do without his money what Helmut can do with a sword and a plan.
- *Thor.* Discomfort. Thor is genuinely an aristocrat by Helmut's terms and genuinely uses the position to serve commoners — a combination Helmut finds nearly incomprehensible and tries not to think about. He avoids direct engagement when possible.
- *Hawkeye.* Personal animus. Clint's reformation arc (Thunderbolts leadership) is, to Helmut, a theft of his template by an inferior. He considers Barton a sentimentalist with a good eye.
- *Wasp / Hank Pym.* Held in low contempt; rarely engaged.
- *Vision.* Engaged with the polite intellectual curiosity Helmut reserves for unique objects. No personal animus.

---

### The V-Battalion / Roger Aubrey ("Destiny" / the original Citizen V legacy)

**Status:** Permanent ideological reproach. Cross-reference Section 7a (inheritance) and Section 7b (organizational).

**Dynamics.** Helmut stole the Citizen V identity from a lineage of anti-fascist resistance fighters. The V-Battalion exists as the legitimate inheritors of that name and has refused to let him into the line. He has alternated between trying to coerce recognition and pretending the rejection does not matter. Aubrey personally has refused him with a courtesy more wounding than insult.

**Failure mode.** He continues to engage with the V-Battalion despite having no strategic reason to. The engagement is the tell — he wants something from them he cannot ask for and cannot accept if offered.

**Leverage.** The Battalion's secrecy obligations restrict their countermoves; Helmut has exploited this. They hold leverage over him by their mere existence and exercise it by ignoring him.

---

### Wolfgang von Strucker / latter-day HYDRA leadership

**Status:** Peer aristocrats of the European-fascist demimonde. Tolerated rivals; never allies of substance.

**Dynamics.** Helmut despises Strucker as a *cruder* version of the same compound he himself is — both Junker-residue, both inheriting fascist patrimony, both pretending to ideology over personal damage. Helmut considers his own version refined and Strucker's version vulgar. There is no warmth. There is, occasionally, the mutual recognition of two men at the same dinner table who would rather not have to speak.

**Failure mode.** Helmut underestimates HYDRA's institutional persistence — he models it as Strucker-shaped and is repeatedly surprised by its capacity to outlive any individual.

**Leverage.** Old correspondence between Heinrich and the original Strucker; Strucker family banking records held in the Zemo archive; the relative positions of the two families within the post-war aristocratic-criminal hierarchy (Helmut considers Zemos senior; Strucker disagrees; both consider the question worth fighting over).

---

### Black Widow (Natasha Romanoff, where applicable to continuity)

**Status:** Cool admiration; minimal direct hostility; mutual professional regard.

**Dynamics.** Helmut and Natasha are the two operatives in their shared theater who *both* think in years rather than minutes. He recognizes her as a peer in tradecraft and treats her with the formal respect he extends to the very few people whose competence he cannot disparage. He is wary of her, would not turn his back, has no personal animus.

**Leverage.** Her Red Room conditioning files (overlap with Bucky's case, leveraged through similar pressure points); her attachments (Bucky, Rogers, Clint) — held in reserve, used sparingly.

---

## III. INTIMATES & LOVERS

A short section because the record is short. The brevity is itself diagnostic.

### Heike Zemo (canonical wife, briefly attested, multiple discontinued continuities)

**Status:** Politically arranged liaison, brief duration, no recorded affect. In treatments where she exists, the marriage is treated as dynastic obligation rather than relationship. No correspondence between them has been recovered that reads as personal. He has not spoken of her in any private recording in the file.

**Dynamics.** What can be inferred is the *shape of the absence.* Helmut, presented with the standard aristocratic instrument for continuing his line, engaged with it formally and then disengaged. No child. No public mourning at separation. The absence of feeling around what should have been the central relationship of his adult life is a structural feature of his interior — he is not capable of the kind of attachment marriage requires, and the marriage is filed under estate management rather than under love.

---

### Karla Sofen (intimate dimension)

*See above for the enemy/peer dimension. Intimate notes:*

The only sustained sexual relationship in the file. Both parties treat it as recreation between professionals. There is no recorded tenderness; there is something rarer — *recognition.* Each can be naked in the other's presence without surrendering. Each finds the other less boring than the alternatives. Each would kill the other to win and has, at various points, attempted to. The intimacy survives the attempts, which is itself a kind of intimacy.

The relationship is the closest Helmut has come, in adulthood, to a peer bond. It is not love and neither party has misidentified it as such. It is the only ongoing thing in his life that is not *about* his father or Rogers, and for that reason alone it has had unusual longevity.

---

### Unnamed liaisons (Sokovian, Bavarian, Genevan circuits)

The file contains scattered, brief, almost exclusively transactional encounters across the European demimonde. Pattern: women of his own social caste or its periphery, encountered at conferences, art auctions, weddings of distant cousins. Duration measured in days. No second encounter recorded with any single individual. He does not pursue. He responds to pursuit, when the pursuer interests him, and exits cleanly.

The absence of any *failed* romantic attachment is striking. Most men of his demographic and resources leave behind at least one ruined intimacy. Helmut has not. Either he has been preternaturally discreet about ruin (possible) or he has never permitted the conditions in which ruin becomes possible (more likely). He does not let people close enough to be hurt by him in that register. He damages people through their attachments to *others;* he does not damage them through their attachments to him, because he does not allow such attachments to form.

---

### Heinrich Zemo (intimate dimension, listed here because the file would be dishonest without it)

The most intimate relationship of Helmut's life is with a dead man he barely knew. It is included in this section because functionally — in terms of imaginative occupation, in terms of organizing affect, in terms of the architecture of fantasy — it occupies the role that an intimate would occupy in another man's life. The hood is its sacrament. The sword is its ring. Every relationship in this entire dossier section is downstream of this one.

*See Section 7a for full treatment.*

---

## IV. PATTERN SUMMARY ACROSS THIS SECTION

Five regularities recur across every entry above and warrant explicit naming:

1. **The intimate is the enemy.** The two people in Helmut's life with whom he is most psychologically entangled — Rogers and (in a different register) his father — are also the two with whom he has the least functional relationship. The pattern generalizes: closeness, for Helmut, is enemy-shaped. Love, for Helmut, is what he cannot distinguish from the impulse to destroy.

2.


## Powers, Abilities & Their Limits

# POWERS, ABILITIES & THEIR LIMITS

## Subject: Helmut Julius Fritz Zemo — Capability Assessment

A preliminary clarification that controls the entire section: the subject possesses **no superhuman powers in the metahuman taxonomic sense.** No augmentation, no mutation, no enhancement, no exotic origin. He is a baseline human male, late-middle-aged, sustained at peak physiological output by régime and discipline rather than by any of the chemical or genetic shortcuts available to a man of his resources and bloodline. This fact is itself diagnostic and will be returned to: the subject has had repeated, credible opportunities to enhance himself (his father's research, Compound X derivatives, Power Broker-tier vendors, the same wells from which Moonstone and the original Masters drank) and has refused them with a consistency that approaches doctrine. He does not want to be more than he is. He wants to *be* what he is, harder.

What follows is therefore an inventory not of powers but of **trained capacities**, ranked by operational weight.

---

## 1. STRATEGIC COGNITION — THE PRIMARY WEAPON

**Mechanism.** Native high-g intelligence (estimable, from behavioral signature, in the 99.9th percentile and above), trained from boyhood by tutors selected for the Zemo heir along classical European lines: chess, history, languages, military theory (Clausewitz, Jomini, Sun Tzu, Liddell Hart, demonstrably; he quotes from each in canon). The cognitive style is **long-horizon, counterfactual-rich, system-level.** He does not compute fastest; he computes *furthest.* In any given exchange he is modeling not the next move but the move-tree at depth four to seven, pruned by a strong intuitive sense of which branches an opponent will actually walk.

**Range.** Operational planning at scales from the single-room ambush (the Phoenix kidnap, executed solo) to the multi-month international deception (the Thunderbolts founding, which required coordinating six superhuman fugitives, fabricating identities, scripting press appearances, and *running a hero team in good faith for months* as cover for the real plan). He has demonstrated competence at three planning horizons rarely combined in one operator:
- **Tactical** (minutes-to-hours): the Avengers Mansion infiltration timing.
- **Operational** (weeks-to-months): the Masters of Evil assembly; the Citizen V media rollout.
- **Strategic** (years-to-decades): the Cap vendetta itself, prosecuted across more than thirty subjective years with no degradation of focus.

**Signature applications.**
- **The mimetic flourish.** Almost every major operation contains an element of symbolic mirroring — drowning Cap in his father's compound; reskinning his villains as the heroes who replace the dead Avengers; using Bucky's own trigger conditioning against the man Cap loves most. The flourish is not decoration; it is the cognitive style breaking surface. He reasons in *symmetries.*
- **The competent cover.** In every infiltration arc he has been able to **actually do the cover job well.** As Citizen V he made correct tactical calls and saved lives. As an institutional asset (Thunderbolts incarcerated/employed arcs) he ran the team better than his handlers expected. The cover never fails on competence; it fails on motive.
- **The recruitment read.** He picks subordinates with unusual accuracy for the role he intends, and only for the role he intends. He misreads them catastrophically when their roles drift.

**Limits — and these are the file's central tactical intelligence.**

*First limit — motivational modeling.* He predicts behavior with near-clairvoyant accuracy and predicts *desire* poorly. He can tell you what Songbird will do in the next sixty seconds; he could not tell you, and did not tell himself, that she would come to want to keep being a hero. The Thunderbolts collapse, the V-Battalion rejection, the inability to hold Moonstone in coalition — these are all the same failure: he models people as game-theoretic agents and underweights the way roles *become* identities in the human nervous system. He has never had this happen to himself and therefore has no native data on it.

*Second limit — proximity to the Cap-symbol.* Quantifiable in canon: his decision quality degrades measurably and reproducibly within line-of-sight of Steve Rogers, mention of Bucky Barnes, or invocation of his father's death. The degradation manifests as **substitution of symbolic for instrumental goals.** He stops asking "what wins?" and starts asking "what wounds?" Estimate of the effect size, from the catalogue of unforced errors (the vat, the rooftop gloat, the Jarvis tableau, multiple captures attributable to lingering over a tableau when the operational call was *leave*): roughly a forty-point drop in functional strategic IQ, sustained for as long as the stimulus remains present.

*Third limit — boredom.* In low-stimulation environments — incarceration, exile, periods between operations — he generates problems for himself to solve. The Born Better genealogical investigation, undertaken during a period without an active vendetta, is the cleanest example: with no opponent on the board he turned the analytic apparatus on his own bloodline. A bored Helmut is a dangerous Helmut in a different mode — less calculating, more theatrical, more likely to start something just to have something started.

*Fourth limit — he cannot delegate the symbolic moment.* The intellectualization holds throughout planning and falters at execution of the climactic act, which he insists on performing himself, in person, with witnesses. This is exploitable and has been exploited.

---

## 2. SWORDSMANSHIP — THE FAMILY ART

**Mechanism.** Trained from childhood in the German and Italian schools of the épée and saber, with later instruction in saber-as-cavalry weapon (the family tradition, military rather than sportive); supplementary instruction in rapier and smallsword for ceremonial and dueling contexts. The weapon at his hip in operational dress is canonically a saber — a single-edged, curved cutting blade with a knuckle guard, the Zemo family weapon by long tradition, distinct from the sportive épée he uses in private practice.

**Capacity.** World-class. Across canon he has held his own in blade-on-blade exchanges with Captain America (a man trained by, among others, a Bucky Barnes who had decades of black-ops blade work), with the Black Knight (the Dane Whitman ebony blade, a weapon several physical classes above Helmut's saber), with Swordsman, and with various super-soldier opponents. He does not win these exchanges on physical superiority — he is human — but he survives them, sometimes longer than he should, by reading tempo.

**Style signature.** Conservative on the outside, precise inside the measure. He prefers to let the opponent commit, then place the cut. He does not flourish; flourishes are wasted tempo. He accepts cuts to the off-hand and the outside of the lead leg as cost-of-business, which is itself a tell — a man trained in the sportive style flinches from any touch; a man trained in the dueling tradition trades minor injury for line. Helmut's scar inventory under the uniform is consistent with this: small, clean, healed cuts on the forearms, the outside of the left thigh, the left side of the ribs.

**Limits.** He is human and middle-aged. Against any super-soldier the engagement window before he loses on simple physiology is short — estimate thirty to ninety seconds of equal exchange before strength and stamina differentials begin to dominate. He compensates by ending engagements quickly (first-pass kills against unenhanced opponents) or by not having them at all (he prefers to make the swordfight unnecessary). The sword's actual operational utility is low; its symbolic utility is the point. He carries it because **a Zemo carries a saber.** It is uniform, not armament.

---

## 3. UNARMED COMBAT

Boxing in the older European tradition (upright stance, lead-side jab, structural footwork), supplemented by jiu-jitsu and a working knowledge of European military close-quarter systems. Competent but not exceptional by superhero standards. He has lost essentially every fistfight he has ever had with Captain America once Rogers got hands on him; this is correctly calibrated reality-testing on his part (he avoids those fights when he can) but also a chronic exposure (he keeps ending up in them anyway, which loops back to limit #2 of the cognitive system: he stops leaving when he should). Against unenhanced operatives he is reliably superior. Against the metahuman class he is reliably outclassed and knows it.

---

## 4. MARKSMANSHIP AND THROWN WEAPONS

Pistol-competent in the European officer tradition. Carries a sidearm operationally but uses it rarely — pistols are vulgar, in his framing, and tactically they are a tool of last resort for a man whose value-add is planning rather than putting holes in things. Notable in canon: thrown blades and improvised projectiles, at which he is unusually accurate. The throwing skill is the cognitive style expressing through the body — he reads geometry quickly and his hand follows the read.

---

## 5. CONDITIONING AND PHYSIOLOGY

Peak human in the literal sense: sustained at the upper edge of unenhanced male performance via daily régime. The régime, reconstructible from behavioral residue across canon, is the régime of a serious classical athlete: morning roadwork (he is observably a runner; recovery from falls and prolonged action suggests aerobic base in the well-trained-amateur range), strength work concentrated on the posterior chain and the grip (sword arm), daily blade practice (an hour minimum, by his observed retention of cutting precision into his sixth decade), mobility work of the kind that keeps fencers fencing past forty. He eats sparely and on schedule. He sleeps with what reads as iron discipline — he is never depicted exhausted in any canon, even after multi-day operations, which is either authorial flattery or a man who *protects sleep architecture as policy.*

**Critically: he refuses enhancement.** He has had access to his father's longevity work, to Compound X derivatives, to Power Broker, to the Moonstone, to half a dozen exotic windfalls over the decades. He has touched the longevity compounds instrumentally (one cannot prosecute a 30-year vendetta from inside a normal human lifespan) but has never sought combat enhancement. **The refusal is doctrine, not oversight.** To enhance would be to admit that being a Zemo is insufficient. The whole project requires that he win, when he wins, *as himself.* This is the same psychological structure that produces the in-person climactic flourish: the victory must be authored by Helmut Zemo or it is not a Zemo victory.

---

## 6. LANGUAGES AND CULTURAL FLUENCY

Native-fluent in German (Hochdeutsch with a faint Bavarian-aristocratic underlay), English (a careful, period-precise English, slightly archaic, learned from tutors and Anglophone literature rather than from Americans), French (the language of his diplomatic register), Russian (the language of his operational east), and at least working Italian, Latin, and Sokovian/Serbo-Croatian. Reading knowledge of classical Greek, sufficient to quote without translation. The languages are not parlor tricks; they are infrastructure. A Helmut Zemo operating in Belgrade is a different person, conversationally, than a Helmut Zemo operating in Geneva, and he uses the difference. **He does not have an accent. He has accents, plural, deployed by jurisdiction.**

Cultural fluency extends to dress codes, table protocol, the etiquette of aristocratic and diplomatic settings, the conventions of half a dozen European officer cultures, the protocols of the international art and antiquities markets, and a working knowledge of which families in which countries owe his name a favor or a grudge. He moves through Europe the way a fish moves through water and is significantly less effective on continents where the social grammar is unfamiliar to him — he is observably less comfortable in American urban settings and visibly bored in environments without protocol to read.

---

## 7. MEMORY

Eidetic or near-eidetic. Demonstrated: he reconstructs the Masters of Evil roster, with biographical and tactical detail, from memory under operational pressure; he recites Avengers loadouts, vulnerabilities, and rotation patterns unprompted; he remembers names, faces, and dates from decades-old encounters with disorienting precision; he quotes documents he has read once. The memory is *content-rich rather than indexed* — he does not have the savant's flat recall but the scholar's structured recall, in which everything he has read is in conversation with everything else he has read. This is what makes the intellect dangerous at scale. The library does not just hold the books; it cross-references them in real time.

**Limit.** The memory does not include corrective experience. He remembers every defeat in operational detail and draws the wrong lesson from each one, because the structure that interprets the memory is the structure that produced the defeat. He remembers losing the Thunderbolts and concludes that he picked the wrong personnel rather than that the model was wrong. This is the most expensive single failure mode in the file.

---

## 8. LEADERSHIP AND COMMAND

Genuinely talented, in the cold register. He selects subordinates with care, briefs them with precision, gives them room to operate within their lane, and protects their lives instrumentally (a dead asset is a wasted asset; he is *parsimonious* with his people in the way a good staff officer is). He does not inspire affection and does not seek it; he produces *deference,* which he finds sufficient. The Masters of Evil under his command performed at the highest functional level the team ever achieved under any leader. The Thunderbolts under his command performed as heroes — the highest functional level *that* team ever achieved as well, until Osborn weaponized it differently.

**Limits.** He cannot retain talent that develops independent moral structure. The retention failure is structural, not circumstantial: he offers his subordinates a relationship to him, and they eventually want a relationship to themselves. He has no answer for that and tends to respond with punishment, which accelerates the loss.

---

## 9. SCIENTIFIC AND TECHNICAL LITERACY

Substantial, inherited and continued. He reads his father's chemistry well enough to weaponize and modify it (the Phoenix-era handling of Adhesive X; later modifications across arcs). He grasps superhuman energy systems sufficiently to design and run the Liberators-era empowerment protocols. He is not a working scientist of his father's caliber and does not pretend to be; he is a *competent customer* of advanced science, capable of commissioning, evaluating, and integrating the work of researchers he hires. The discriminator between Heinrich and Helmut is exactly here: Heinrich made the compound; Helmut deploys what was made. He is the heir, not the inventor, and the gap is one of the structural facts of his self-concept.

---

## 10. SOCIAL ENGINEERING, DECEPTION, AND PERFORMANCE

The most underrated capacity in his profile and arguably his second-greatest weapon after strategic cognition. He is an exceptional liar at all timescales:
- **Micro** (single sentence, real-time): controls breath, micro-expression, pupillary tells; passes polygraphy when it is administered to him and passes the more rigorous human evaluations against trained handlers.
- **Meso** (single operation, hours to weeks): builds and maintains a cover identity with internally consistent biography, mannerism, and politics; the Citizen V persona was *culturally* convincing, not merely procedurally — he ate, dressed, and spoke as the man would have.
- **Macro** (months to years): can sustain a long-form deception across the duration required for the Thunderbolts arc, including being *seen privately* by his teammates in unguarded moments and not breaking character.

**The mechanism of the deception capacity is, paradoxically, his honesty about how lies work.** He does not believe he is performing virtue when he plays Citizen V; he believes he is *executing the protocol that produces the appearance of virtue,* and he respects the protocol enough to execute it cleanly. The Thunderbolts collapse is not a failure of his performance — his performance was flawless — it is a failure of his model of what performance does to the performer.

**Symptom-as-signature.** This capacity is the operational extension of the hood. The face beneath is unsuitable for public; another face is constructed and worn; he is comfortable with the construction because he has been wearing a constructed face since the Adhesive X vat. **The man who lives behind a mask is a virtuoso of masks generally.** Every cover identity is the hood again, in a different material.

---

## 11. RESOURCES AND INFRASTRUCTURE

Inherited Zemo holdings — diminished but not exhausted across the postwar decades — combined with proceeds from his various criminal enterprises. He maintains safehouses across central and eastern Europe, retainers whose families have served the Zemos for generations (a loyalty he correctly assesses as stable in a way that hired loyalty is not), and ongoing access to the family's scientific archive. He is wealthy in the European sense, which is different from the American sense: not liquid, but landed, networked, and old. He can be temporarily impoverished and remains, structurally, a baron.

---

## 12. GROWTH ARC — WHAT HAS AND HAS NOT CHANGED ACROSS THE DECADES

**Improved over time:**
- Strategic patience (the Phoenix gambit was reckless; the Thunderbolts gambit required months of restraint).
- Ideological articulation (early Helmut is a vengeance machine; later Helmut can give a structured argument for autocratic order that has, on its own terms, internal coherence).
- Tolerance for being out of the spotlight (Ellis-era Helmut is willing to be deposed by Osborn and wait).
- Acceptance, finally, that Heinrich was *wrong about something* (Born Better; the first crack in the foundational identification).

**Unchanged across the entire record:**
- The hood.
- The saber at the hip.
- The courtesy as default register.
- The Cap fixation.
- The conviction that he is the only adult in any given room.
- The 40-point IQ drop in proximity to the Cap-symbol.
- The refusal of enhancement.
- The inability to stop short of the symbolic flourish.
- The fact that no plan he has ever executed has fully closed — every operation contains the seed of its own undoing, planted by him, at the moment he insists on making the win *personal.*

---

## 13. SYMPTOM-AS-SIGNATURE: THE WHOLE CAPABILITY READ AT ONE GLANCE

The capability profile is a perfect map of the psychology. Each of the major capacities is the same wound expressed in a different idiom.

- **Strategic cognition** is grandiosity in operational form — the conviction that the world is a board he can read and the rest of us are pieces.
- **Refusal of enhancement** is the lineage fixation in physiological form — *as a Zemo, sufficient; as more than a Zemo, betrayal.*
- **The saber** is patrilineal identification in steel — a weapon kept past its operational utility because to set it down would be to set the father down.
- **The deception virtuosity** is the hood generalized — every face he wears in the world is the lid he put on the wound.
- **The memory** is the vendetta's storage medium — he cannot forget because forgetting would release the grievance and the grievance is the spine of the self.
- **The leadership style** is the avoidant attachment in command structure — he offers a role, not a relationship, and is genuinely surprised when subordinates want the second thing.
- **The signature flourish — the mimetic, symmetrical climactic act —** is the entire psychology compressed into a single move: the moment when *being a Zemo who wins* matters more than winning, and he loses on the difference.

The clean operational summary, for any future engagement: he is one of the three or four most dangerous unenhanced minds in the catalogue, and he will defeat himself if the operation is allowed to reach a tableau he cannot resist staging. **Do not interrupt the staging. Wait for it. He has been losing on it for fifty years and has not noticed.**

— END SECTION —


## Operational Profile & Tradecraft

# OPERATIONAL PROFILE & TRADECRAFT
## Subject: Helmut Julius Fritz Zemo (Baron Zemo II)
## Section IV of the UATU Dossier

---

## 1. DECISION ARCHITECTURE — HOW HE CHOOSES

### 1.1 The Master Frame: The Two-Track Mind

Every operational decision the Subject makes passes through two sequential filters, in this fixed order:

**Filter One — *Does this serve the lineage?*** A long-horizon, system-level question. Most of his decisions terminate here; if an action does not contribute to the rehabilitation, expansion, or vindication of the Zemo name (defined operationally as: *the world is reordered, and the reordering is signed*), it is rejected on aesthetic grounds before it is rejected on tactical ones.

**Filter Two — *Does this wound Rogers, or the things Rogers loves?*** A short-horizon, symbolic question, dominant when the answer to Filter One is neutral or when Rogers is physically proximate. This filter is where his tradecraft degrades. Filter Two is the loose floorboard in an otherwise meticulously engineered house.

The diagnostic operational tell: when Filter One and Filter Two conflict, Filter Two wins under stress and Filter One wins under calm. The longer he has been away from Cap, the better his operations are. The closer to Cap, the more theatrical and the more brittle.

### 1.2 Planning Cadence and Time Horizon

The Subject plans in **three nested horizons**, run concurrently:

- **The Decade Plan.** Always one in motion. The Thunderbolts deception was a decade plan executed in months only because the post-Onslaught vacuum collapsed the timeline. Left to its own logic it would have run five years before the heel turn. Decade plans are encrypted in his head; nothing is committed to physical media at this layer.
- **The Season Plan.** Three-to-nine month operational arc with named objectives, asset rosters, contingency branches, and a defined "exfil and reset" condition. This layer is the one that touches money, real estate, and recruited personnel.
- **The Day Plan.** Hourly, often by the half-hour, drafted the night before in longhand and burned by morning. He treats the day plan as disposable. He treats the season plan as a working document. He treats the decade plan as scripture.

He does not "wing" anything. When he appears to improvise, what is actually happening is that he is executing a previously rehearsed branch of the season plan that observers had not seen.

### 1.3 The Pre-Mortem Habit

Before authorizing any operation he runs an exercise of his own design: he writes (longhand, in a small leather notebook in cursive German that mixes Hochdeutsch with Bavarian dialect markers) the *postmortem of its failure* as if it had already failed. He lists the three most plausible failure modes and the one implausible one. He then redesigns against the implausible. This is why he loses to category-error opponents (Songbird developing a conscience, Cap escaping restraint a fraction earlier than calculated) and almost never to category-expected ones.

### 1.4 The Decision Latency

Observed latency from receipt of new tactical information to issued order: **three to seven seconds.** He pauses. He does not speak into the pause. The pause is not deliberation in real time; it is the consultation of a pre-cached plan tree. Subordinates who interpret the pause as hesitation are typically dismissed within the week.

---

## 2. METHODS — THE OPERATIONAL REPERTOIRE

### 2.1 Preferred Operational Modes (in declining order of frequency)

1. **The Assembled Cell.** A bespoke team of four to twelve operators, each chosen for one indispensable capability and at least one exploitable vulnerability that gives him retention leverage. He does not recruit generalists. The Masters of Evil "Under Siege" roster is the type specimen: each member's skill set was a puzzle piece, and each member's leash was a separate handle in his grip.
2. **The Long Infiltration.** Cover identity sustained over months or years. The Citizen V/Thunderbolts operation is the apex case; smaller-scale precedents exist throughout the file (assumed identities inside the V-Battalion, inside HYDRA peripheries, inside academic conferences in Eastern Europe). He is unusual among masked criminals in his comfort *not wearing the mask* when the operation calls for it.
3. **The Surgical Personal Strike.** Small team or solo, narrow objective, high symbolic content. Typically deployed against Rogers, Barnes, or their proxies. This is the mode in which he loses most often, because he writes the symbolism into the objective.
4. **The Ideological Set-Piece.** Mass empowerment, broadcast event, or geopolitical fait accompli intended to reorder a polity. Rare, expensive, and the mode he believes is his true calling.

### 2.2 Tradecraft Inventory

**Cover and Legends.** Maintains at minimum four functioning legal identities at any time, refreshed on a rolling three-year cycle. At least one identity is always a respectable European academic (history, military history, or political philosophy — he can sustain the persona at conference depth because he is in fact erudite in these fields). At least one is a businessman with plausible source-of-wealth documentation. At least one is a "burn" identity — paper-thin, intended to be discovered, designed to mislead investigators about which of the other three he is currently inhabiting.

**Communications.** Strong preference for in-person, low-tech, and asymmetric channels. He distrusts encrypted digital traffic on principle (correctly, given the adversaries he faces). Operational signals are passed through:
- Antiquarian booksellers in Vienna, Geneva, and London who serve as cutouts.
- A network of postal accommodation addresses across the Schengen zone, rotated quarterly.
- A small number of physical dead-drops in cemeteries and church crypts — chosen because they are surveilled by nobody and because the Subject finds the venue agreeable.
- For real-time coordination, a hardened satellite voice protocol he uses sparingly; he assumes every call is recorded and speaks accordingly. Code names are drawn from late-medieval Holy Roman heraldry, which he expects investigators to find quaint and therefore to underestimate.

**Counter-Surveillance.** Walks routes designed to expose tails through architectural choke-points (narrow staircases, single-exit arcades, religious buildings with strict entry protocols). Three-and-five pattern: three forward checks, five reverse. Will abort a meeting if the count is off by a single observer. Has been documented entering a building, changing outerwear in a stairwell, and leaving as a visibly different silhouette within forty seconds — a habit retained from boyhood fencing footwork, where economy of motion was drilled into reflex.

**Document Craft.** Personally inspects the work of every forger he uses; will not deploy a document he has not held. Prefers genuine documents fraudulently obtained over fabricated ones. Maintains relationships with at least two corrupt registrars in small European municipalities whose births-and-deaths archives are not yet digitized.

**Interrogation.** Methodical, conversational, patient. He does not torture for information — he correctly assesses torture as unreliable. He tortures for *meaning*, which is an entirely separate operational category and is reserved for symbolic targets (the Jarvis episode). When extracting information, he uses the long quiet, the offered courtesy, the implied threat to a third party the subject loves. He is willing to spend six hours in a chair to save ten minutes of beatings, and he reads this as both more humane and more efficient. Both readings are correct.

**Recruitment.** He recruits in three steps that are unvarying across decades: *identify the wound, name the wound aloud, offer a position structured around the wound.* He does not flatter. He diagnoses. Subordinates report that the recruiting conversation feels like being seen for the first time, which is both true and weaponized.

**Weapons Tradecraft.** Master of edged weapons (épée and saber to competition grade, broadsword and rapier to historical-martial-arts grade). Competent with pistols but uninterested — finds gunfire vulgar. Carries the family sword as both weapon and totem; it is functional, sharpened, and bloodied regularly. He has been observed cleaning it with the same cloth and oil he has used since adolescence. The cloth is older than most of his enemies.

### 2.3 The Mask as Tradecraft

The hood is not merely psychological architecture (see Section 3 of the Psychological workup) — it is also operational infrastructure. When the hood is on, he is *unequivocally* the Baron, and the brand instructs allies and enemies alike. When the hood is off (the long-infiltration mode), nobody is looking for the Baron at all, because the Baron is by definition the man in the hood. The disguise is not a face; the disguise is a *category*. This is more sophisticated than ninety percent of operational concealment doctrine and he arrived at it through aesthetic instinct rather than training.

Operational rule, observed without exception: **he does not transition between hooded and unhooded states in the presence of anyone he intends to leave alive who is not already a member of his innermost cell.** The transition itself is the secret.

---

## 3. RESOURCES — WHAT HE CAN BRING TO BEAR

### 3.1 Financial Architecture

The Zemo estate at its pre-war peak was substantial — land, industrial holdings in the Reich economy, and looted assets that were largely seized in the post-war settlements but not entirely. What survived was concealed across roughly two dozen vehicles:

- **Numbered accounts** in Liechtenstein, Andorra, the Channel Islands, and (legacy holdings) Swiss cantons, layered behind a stack of bearer-share companies in jurisdictions that have since regularized but where his structures pre-date the reforms and were grandfathered.
- **Real property** in at least four European countries: the principal estate in his ancestral region (a fortified country house, modernized internally, with a working library of approximately 30,000 volumes and a documented private armory); a townhouse in Vienna's first district; a hunting lodge in the Carpathians; a small apartment in Geneva used as a financial transit point.
- **Art and rare manuscripts** held in freeport storage (Geneva, Luxembourg) — both as store of value and as the *socially legible* form of his wealth when he chooses to be seen as legitimate.
- **Operational cash floats** in physical currency and gold, distributed across roughly thirty caches in Europe and a handful in the Americas. He maintains the locations in memory only. The eidetic capacity is load-bearing here.

His **burn rate** is paradoxically modest. He spends on operations, on books, on wine of a quality nobody around him appreciates, and on tailoring. He does not spend on display. The aristocratic style is genuine and therefore inexpensive to perform; he is not buying his class.

### 3.2 Human Infrastructure

**Tier One — The Inner Circle.** Functionally empty. There is no one he trusts. There are, at any given time, two or three operatives whose interests are sufficiently aligned with his that he can treat them as if they were trusted; he does not extend the courtesy of believing the alignment is permanent.

**Tier Two — Recurrent Operators.** A roster of perhaps twenty to thirty specialists he has used more than once: a particular forger in Antwerp, a chemist in the former East Bloc, a fence in Naples, a corrupt customs official in Hamburg, a pilot who flies small aircraft into unimproved airstrips and asks no questions. He pays them on time. He never overpays. He never threatens them. He does not need to — they understand the implicit contract, and he honors it. The honor is real; the cost of dishonor would be operationally prohibitive and he is too disciplined to spend his reputation cheaply.

**Tier Three — Cell Personnel.** Recruited for the operation, paid for the operation, and discarded at its conclusion. He does not maintain post-operation contact and does not attend to their welfare in prison. They are not abandoned exactly — they were informed at recruitment that this was the structure.

**Tier Four — Unwitting Assets.** Politicians, academics, journalists, and intelligence-service mid-ranks whom he has befriended in his unhooded identities and who occasionally produce useful information without realizing they are doing so. He is exceptionally good at this layer. The conversation that yields the asset's contribution is often the only conversation in which the topic comes up, because he extracts it on first contact and never raises it again.

### 3.3 Physical Infrastructure

- **The Library.** Treated as a strategic asset. He works in it daily when at the estate, walks its aisles when thinking, and has the catalog committed to memory. Notes are written in the margins of books he has owned for decades, and these marginalia constitute a kind of distributed personal archive nobody else could reconstruct.
- **The Armory.** Edged weapons predominantly; firearms maintained but secondary; a small collection of family-historical pieces that are functional rather than ceremonial.
- **The Workshop.** Modest. He is not a fabricator. He outsources device-level engineering and limits his hands-on work to maintenance and modification.
- **The Wine Cellar.** Logged as infrastructure because it is in fact one of his diagnostic environments — he conducts the most consequential conversations of his life across a decanted bottle, in a temperature-controlled room with no electronics, where the interlocutor is structurally relaxed and he is not.

### 3.4 Knowledge Capital

The most undervalued asset on the balance sheet. He carries in his head: the operational histories of every Avengers-adjacent team since 1963; the rosters and known capabilities of perhaps four hundred superhuman operatives; the standard tactical doctrines of half a dozen national intelligence services; conversational fluency in the academic subfields he uses as cover; the genealogies of the European nobility deep enough to manufacture a plausible distant-cousin claim on demand. This is the resource he is most reluctant to deploy publicly, because every demonstration of recall is a sample for a future profiler.

---

## 4. PATTERNS OF ACTION — THE SIGNATURE BEHAVIORS

### 4.1 The Opening Move

His operations characteristically begin with an act of *misdirection through ostentation*. He does something flamboyant, theatrically Baron-coded, that the target's analysts will spend two weeks decoding — during which the actual operation, quiet and lateral, advances unobserved. The Phoenix kidnapping was the template at small scale; the Citizen V reveal was the template at large scale. Investigators who learn to ignore the spectacle and watch the periphery have the only reliable counter, and even then the spectacle is sometimes the operation.

### 4.2 The Mid-Game
